Current Affairs Commentary

Prospects for Sino-Japanese Diplomacy

— All

Adjusting Sino-Japanese relations is the highest call of today's general society and the most ardent desire of peace-loving nations. However, since the start of negotiations, several months have passed, and not only has there been no progress in mutual understanding, but the situation has become increasingly serious. The Suiyuan Incident erupted, followed by the Qingdao dispute, almost leading to the inability to conduct diplomatic negotiations. This is a matter of great regret for those who care about the overall situation in East Asia.

We have also pondered anxiously and thoughtfully, wondering why the adjustment work is so difficult to complete. Where does the reason lie? Examining past facts, it is not difficult to understand the truth thoroughly. It lies in our adherence to the principle of mutual respect for sovereignty, while they regard military threats as their forte. Pursuing closeness with such goals is like going south while heading north, utterly impossible. Even a three-year-old child knows that the impasse is very difficult to break.

When Foreign Minister Zhang began negotiations with Ambassador Arita, he already clarified our country's position of maintaining territorial integrity. Under this principle, the first issue to be resolved was the Northeast problem. However, after Arita considered that the time was not yet ripe, Foreign Minister Zhang also knew that this move would not be easy to accomplish suddenly. In order to show the genuine sincerity of adjusting national relations, he resolutely abandoned his original position and temporarily set aside the matter, focusing only on finding ways to eliminate the state of affairs hindering the administrative integrity of Hebei, Chahar, and Inner Mongolia. However, what was the Japanese side's response to our excessive sincerity? How was their continued program of aggression reflected in reality? This is the first point that shows our side cannot be blamed for lacking sincerity. The biggest criticism the Japanese side makes against us today is the agitation of national sentiment. For a country with 400 million people, subjected to continuous damage over the years, to remain silent like cicadas in winter or tremble like horses facing a phantom enemy is not easy. In order to maintain genuine peace between the two countries, the government has repeatedly admonished and suppressed such sentiments. The people, understanding this intention, have also had to restrain their indignant emotions in order to seek improvement in the situation. Such a peace-loving nation is rare in the world. Unfortunately, they still consider it insufficient, constantly casting negative impressions and increasing the stimulation of our people, creating irreparable antipathy. When water overflows, the responsibility lies where it belongs. Even a government that strives for tolerance will lose its ability to control. This is the second point that shows our side has exhausted all means to adjust national relations.

In short, the situation has reached a point where one can only sigh in dismay. If the Japanese side truly has no intention of starting a war lightly, it should first selectively resolve local incidents to an appropriate extent, and then gradually seek to improve overall national relations as the world situation evolves. If they still fail to understand our country's situation and insist on going their own way, even believing that they can adopt an automatic policy toward China, as stated in the recent Three Provinces Conference, then the future will be fraught with dangerous changes, beyond imagination. It must be understood that our country's concessions have reached their final limit. The people all have a firm determination, deeply ashamed of the insults they have suffered and anxious about impending disaster. The entire country is sharpening its swords, preparing only for calm and determined struggle.

Baldwin Explains to the House of Commons the Process of the King's Marriage Proposal; Everything is Still Undecided; Churchill Speaks with Embarrassment

(London) Prime Minister Baldwin made a statement in the House of Commons this afternoon regarding the constitutional dispute, stating, "The government has not offered any other advice besides presenting the King with the issue of a morganatic marriage. My personal conversations with the King were purely private and informal." Baldwin's statement, in response to the question raised by Labour Party leader Attlee last Friday, should dispel many rumors, including those mentioned in Churchill's statement yesterday. After Baldwin's statement, Churchill attempted to rise and speak, criticizing the government, but was forced to sit down in silence due to opposition from the crowd. Liberal MP Lambert then asked Baldwin whether he was aware that the House of Commons expressed deep sympathy for him. After Lambert finished speaking, the entire chamber cheered in agreement. Subsequently, Baldwin answered Churchill's question, stating that the King had not yet made a decision and said, "All these issues were not initially raised by the government. In fact, during a conversation between the King and myself, the King himself told me that he intended to marry Mrs. Simpson after she was free. This shows that the King has held this intention for some time. After the King decides on the path he wants to take, he will naturally inform the government and the various dominions. At that time, each government will try to offer appropriate advice on the King's decision, to fulfill their responsibilities. Before concluding this statement, I should first express the feeling of the entire House, which is that at present, we have deep and respectful sympathy for the King." After Baldwin finished speaking, the entire chamber cheered loudly, expressing their agreement.

Labour Party leader Attlee then spoke, stating that the people of the country would undoubtedly agree with Baldwin's views and requested Baldwin to disclose as much information about the matter as possible to satisfy the expectations of the country. Baldwin immediately replied that the King had not yet made a decision, so there was no information to disclose. Churchill then rose and spoke, asking Baldwin whether he could guarantee that no firm steps would be taken before the House of Commons received all the information about the matter. While Churchill was speaking, some people shouted "Shame" and "Sit down" to interrupt him. Churchill continued his speech, asking Baldwin not to forget that this incident affected the entire constitution. At this point, others in the chamber shouted again to stop Churchill from speaking. However, Churchill still spoke loudly amidst the disturbances, saying, "If the House of Commons does not allow me to ask questions, the result will make my words even more important." Then the Speaker asked Churchill to be as simple as possible when asking questions. Churchill ignored this and reiterated the above request. However, the noise in the chamber at that time made Churchill's words impossible to hear, so he had no choice but to sit down in silence. Baldwin replied to Churchill amidst cheers, saying, "I find it difficult to answer Churchill's question at present because I do not yet know what the King wants to decide." (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

The King's Marriage Problem is Still Under Careful Study; The Element of Abdication is Reduced

(London) From morning today, the public gathered on Downing Street and other important locations despite the severe cold, watching the comings and goings of ministers and other dignitaries. The King's official car carried Mr. Monckton, legal advisor to the Duchy of Cornwall, from Fort Belvedere Palace to No. 10 Downing Street, where it remained for two and a half hours. It is reported that before Mr. Monckton arrived, Colonial Secretary MacDonald visited Prime Minister Baldwin with a stack of documents and left after ten minutes. Sir Peacock, the tax revenue manager for the Duchy of Cornwall, visited the Prime Minister after Monckton. The King is currently staying at Fort Belvedere Palace. There was no activity there last night. The lights, which usually did not go out until four or five in the morning after the crisis, were not seen after two o'clock last night. (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

(London) The Attorney General of the Duchy of Cornwall, namely the King's confidant, Monckton, went to the Prime Minister's office at 10:15 AM this morning and had a conversation with the Prime Minister for two and a half hours before leaving. In addition, twenty Conservative Members of Parliament from both the House of Lords and the House of Commons held a special meeting to discuss the constitutional disputes caused by the marriage problem. (Havas dispatch, 7th)

(London) It is now reliably learned that King Edward VIII is considering flying to Cannes, France, to meet with Mrs. Simpson to discuss the issue of abdication. It is also learned that the King is considering indefinitely postponing the marriage at the request of three or five close friends. The odds on abdication have decreased from two to one. (National News Agency dispatch, 7th)

(London) It is known today that Queen Mary and members of the Royal Family are all afraid that the King might suddenly take a plane to secretly meet with Mrs. Simpson in the South of France. The Queen Mother had a meeting with the King from 4:30 PM to 7:20 PM on Sunday afternoon, and it is said that there was a fierce argument. The Queen Mother strongly advised the King, for the sake of his personal conduct and the teachings of his ancestors, not to prioritize personal desires over the responsibilities of the nation. However, the King said that he had the right to choose his own way of life and therefore refused the Queen Mother's advice. At that time, the King's face was haggard and he was very angry. Members of the Royal Family all believed that the King had decided to abdicate, and the Queen Mother, considering the King's attitude, also felt that abdication was better. It is said that the Queen Mother's spirit has been overly strained and she is unable to support herself. She has looked old in recent days, but she is still able to deal with the crisis with a brave attitude. According to those close to the Royal Family, the Queen Mother weeps day and night, her mind is dazed, and she does not believe that the people's love for the Royal Family, built up by her late husband George and her own life's efforts, will be overthrown in one day, and she feels infinite pain in her heart. (National News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Only the Duke of Cornwall's Flag Flies Over the King's Palace; Newspapers Consider it a Sign of Abdication; Airplanes and Royal Cars Come and Go

(London) According to custom, the Monarch's flag (red, blue, and gold) should be flown wherever the King resides. However, Marlborough House, where Queen Mary resides, still flies this flag. As for Fort Belvedere Palace, where King Edward VIII resides, the flag waving in the wind from the tower is the Duke of Cornwall's flag (the flag is black with fifteen gold ancient coins), not the Monarch's flag. The newspapers have commented on this one after another, believing that the King's willingness to fly the Duke's flag is not a good sign. There were few people going to Fort Belvedere Palace today. At noon, two old women arrived at the palace gate together in a car. They handed a large envelope to the guards, simply saying that it was "to be presented to the King." (Havas dispatch, 7th)

(London) The King is currently residing at Fort Belvedere Palace in Windsor Forest. The palace is closely guarded by the Royal Guards and local police. Two guards are stationed in front of the gate. Cars are allowed to pass as usual on the nearby road, but they are not allowed to stop in front of the gate. However, many people still deliberately slow down when passing the palace, wanting to catch a glimpse of the situation inside in that instant. At dawn today, a plane flew near the palace, quite close to the ground, and then flew away. The police tried to find out the origin of the plane, but they were unable to see clearly due to the hazy weather. By dusk, pedestrians had disappeared on the road near the palace. The King's car drove out of the palace at 5:30 PM, the curtains were lowered, and it was impossible to know who was inside. (National News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Soviet Congress Concludes; New Constitution Passed and Effective; Important Amendments Passed; Protects Private Property and Implements Democracy; Conditions for Declaring War Also Improved

(Moscow) The Eighth All-Soviet Special Congress held its final decision-making meeting in the Kremlin at 4:00 PM today, passing the full amended text of the draft of the new Soviet Constitution. Stalin rose to deliver a report on behalf of the Review Committee. The entire body of delegates and Laobao cheered, applauded, and cheered.

Stalin said in his speech, "The work of the Review Committee has been completed. The amended draft of the new Constitution has been distributed to all the delegates of the Congress. Therefore, the Congress Hall is well aware of its content. The Review Committee has cited 43 amendments and modified 32 articles of the original draft. The other 114 articles remain unchanged from the original draft.

"The first is the amendment to Article 8 of the original draft. The original draft said, "Collective farms occupy land for a period of use without restriction, that is, permanent occupation." The amended provision says, "Collective farms occupy land for free use, and there is no restriction in the interval, that is, permanent occupation." The significance of this amendment is clear and does not need to be explained.

"The second is the amendment to Article 10. The original draft stated, "Personal property such as citizens' work income, savings, household items and appliances in their residences and household-affiliated economy, and personal items for use and enjoyment are protected by law." The amended text states, "The right to personal property such as citizens' work income, savings, household items and appliances in their residences and household-affiliated economy, and personal items for use or enjoyment, as well as the right to inheritance of citizens' personal property, are protected by law." The significance of this amendment is clear and does not need to be explained further.

"The third amendment concerns Article 35. The original text of this article stated that the National Council is organized by representatives elected by the Supreme Council of each federal republic and autonomous republic, and by the Soviet representatives of the toilers of each autonomous province. Each federal republic sends 10 representatives, each autonomous republic sends 5 representatives, and each autonomous province sends 2 representatives." The amended text reads, "The National Council is composed of representatives elected by Soviet citizens of each federal and autonomous republic, each autonomous province, and each national district through universal suffrage. Each federal republic elects 25 representatives, each autonomous republic elects 11 representatives, each autonomous province elects 5 representatives, and each national district elects 1 representative." Thus, this article is fully in line with the equality of the two houses and the principle of equal use of democratic methods to form.

"The fourth is the amendment to Article 40. The original draft of this article stated, "The laws passed by the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union shall be signed and promulgated by the Chairman of the Supreme Soviet and the Secretary of the Presidium." The amended text states, "The laws passed by the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union shall be signed and promulgated in the languages of each federal republic by the Chairman of the Supreme Soviet and the Secretary of the Presidium." The significance of this amendment is clear and does not need to be explained. As a result, all laws will be promulgated in eleven languages.

"The fifth is the amendment to Article 48. The original draft stipulates that the Supreme Soviet shall have four vice-chairmen. The amendment changes it to eleven vice-chairmen, which is equal to the number of federal republics.

"The sixth is the amendment to Article 77, which suggests that a People's Commissariat for the National Defense Industry be added to the existing all-Union People's Commissariats. This amendment does not need to be explained.

"The last amendment concerns Article 49癸. The original draft said, "During the adjournment of the Supreme Soviet, the Presidium shall declare war if the Soviet Union is attacked by armed forces." The amended text says, "During the adjournment of the Supreme Soviet, the Presidium shall declare war if the Soviet Union is attacked by armed forces, or if it is necessary to fulfill the obligations of an international mutual assistance treaty to resist aggression." (Heavy applause) This article was amended in response to French protests.)

"Other amendments are not of a substantive nature and are purely of a linguistic nature, so there is no need to analyze them in detail."

After Stalin's speech, Chairman Andreyeff read out each article of the Constitution and put it to a vote. It took more than an hour, and each article was unanimously passed, interspersed with applause. After each article was passed, the chairman put the entire text to a general vote, and the result was unanimously passed by the entire audience.

After the full text of the new constitution was passed, the entire audience burst into thunderous cheers and applause, celebrating together. The entire audience stood up and congratulated Stalin and the Presidium. Voices in different languages were raised everywhere in the audience, cheering Stalin, the creator of the constitution and the leader of the people, for a long time. After the cheers, the Congress sang the Internationale together.

Afterwards, the Congress ordered the Soviet Central Executive Committee to formulate and approve the election regulations and election procedures of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union in accordance with the new constitution. The Congress also resolved that December 5 should be designated as National Day in commemoration of the new constitution. Thus, this historic Congress, which discussed and passed the new constitution, closed amid renewed cheers congratulating Stalin and the party and government leaders. The new constitution took effect on the same day. (TASS dispatch, 5th)

Pan-American Conference: The United States Promotes Neutrality Policy, Establishes a Consultation Convention, and Forms Two Committees to Ensure Peaceful Resolution of Disputes Among Nations

(Washington) The State Department announced today that Secretary of State Hull will propose at the Pan-American Conference tomorrow the establishment of an American Consultation Convention to adjust existing treaties among American countries. Its powers are twofold: to determine the state of war and to decide whether non-belligerent countries can invoke neutrality laws. Hull's motive in presenting this case is to promote the U.S. Neutrality Act to all republics in the Western Hemisphere. The preamble to this convention includes the Kellogg-Briand Pact initiated by Kellogg and Briand, the American Conciliation Convention signed in Washington on January 5, 1929, the Arbitration Convention, and the Saavedra Lamas Pact signed in the capital of Chile on October 10, 1933. It also organizes a committee consisting of the prime ministers or foreign ministers of the American countries. If disputes arise among countries, mediation will be conducted before invoking the treaty. (National Telegram, 6th)

Capital of Argentina: The U.S. delegation to the American Peace Conference recently proposed that countries in North, Central, and South America sign a neutrality convention so that when disputes arise among the signatory countries, they can be resolved peacefully. It also establishes two committees: one is a permanent committee composed of the foreign ministers of the signatory countries, and the other is the American Advisory Committee, whose task is to ensure the implementation of the neutrality agreement. The draft convention proposes that when disputes arise among North, Central, and South American countries, the parties concerned should resolve them through diplomatic channels or jointly organize investigation, mediation, and arbitration committees. If a compromise cannot be reached, an appeal must be made to the American Advisory Committee. If disputes still cannot be resolved, even if war breaks out, all neutral countries, that is, all signatory countries other than the parties concerned, should issue orders to prohibit the transportation of military supplies to the warring countries and should refuse to provide financial assistance. In addition, each neutral country may decide on various commercial sanctions to deal with the warring countries. (Havas Telegram, 6th)

Mexico Allows Trotsky to Reside

Mexico City: Leon Trotsky, the exiled leader of the Soviet Russian Communist Party's anti-faction, was formerly restricted in his movements in Norway after the Soviet Russian counter-revolutionary case occurred. Recently, through the mediation of his follower Rivera, the Mexican Foreign Ministry has specially approved his residence in Mexico. Although the General Confederation of Labor and other workers' groups expressed their opposition, it was ultimately ineffective. The Ministry recently issued a statement on this matter, stating, "Mexico has always adhered faithfully to the principles of international law, especially the right of political prisoners to seek asylum in other countries, which is a matter of pride. In accordance with this principle, Trotsky is specially allowed to reside here. It is an overestimation to say that Trotsky's arrival here will cause internal strife or lead to international disputes. On the contrary, the government will monitor Trotsky at all times and prevent him from interfering in internal affairs." The statement concluded by saying that, as of now, Trotsky himself has not formally requested to reside in Mexico from the Mexican government. (Havas Telegram, 7th)

Hankou City: Methods for Citizens to Donate Funds to Support Suiyuan; One-Day Campaign Implemented in Ten Categories; Central and Five Other Banks Designated to Receive Payments

Hankou Communication: Hankou citizens are enthusiastically donating funds to support Suiyuan. However, the one-day campaign was deemed to have too many categories and relatively complicated procedures. Therefore, the "Hankou City National Contribution One-Day Campaign Promotion Committee" has been established to coordinate the efforts. Its outline has been stipulated, dividing the city's citizens into ten categories: (1) civil servants, teachers, clerks, and workers with salary income; (2) freelancers; (3) profits from companies, firms, factories, and stores; (4) real estate income earners; (5) amusement venues; (6) students; (7) workers in various industries; (8) farmers; (9) women; (10) those without fixed occupations and organizations. Regarding the collection methods, for the first category, letters will be sent to the persons in charge of various agencies and organizations, and the principals or managers of various companies, firms, factories, and stores, asking them to deduct one-thirtieth of their monthly salary. For the second category, the average is one-thirtieth of the monthly income or one-three hundred and sixty-fifth of the annual income. For the third category, 1. 5% will be deducted from the total revenue of one day's business income. 2. For shops that do not have invoices, receipts, or cash flow books for verification, the estimated method will be used to determine the total amount of one day's business income and charge an appropriate percentage as one day's income. 3. Merchants will use one day's commission income. 4. Silver and money businesses will charge one-three hundred and sixty-fifth of the total net profit for the year. For the fourth category, one-third of the amount of the housing donation in December 25 will be collected, and the tenants will pay in advance and issue receipts to offset the rent. For the fifth category, collect the full amount of one day's business income. For the sixth category, all students will use one day's pocket money, candy expenses, and savings from dieting. For the seventh category, workers in various industries will use one day's wage income. For the eighth category, farmers will use one-three hundred and sixty-fifth of their annual harvest income. For the ninth category, women will use one month's savings from cosmetics expenses. For the tenth category, those without fixed occupations and organizations will donate one day's expenses according to their economic situation. The methods for soliciting donations from wealthy and well-to-do households will be determined separately, and those who voluntarily donate more than the standard amount will be allowed to do so.

As for the collection and delivery procedures, for the salary income portion, the central agencies will be collected by their responsible officials, and the municipal agencies will be collected by the heads of the municipal government and its affiliated agencies according to their nature. Various companies, firms, factories, stores, and groups will be collected by their responsible persons and submitted to the affiliated guilds for transfer. Those without guild organizations will be sent to the designated collection points. For the freelance portion, it will be collected and transferred by the various guilds. For the real estate income portion, it will be collected by the owners' assembly office. For the amusement venue portion, it will be collected by the theater guild. For the student portion, it will be collected by the education association in conjunction with the principals of each school. For the worker portion, it will be collected by the various industry guilds, and detailed measures will be determined separately. For the farmer portion, it will be collected by the district farmers' associations, and detailed measures will be determined separately through joint discussions of the district farmers' associations. For the women's portion, it will be discussed by the association in conjunction with the Municipal Women's Association and the Women's Relief Association. For those without fixed occupations and organizations, it will be conducted through door-to-door solicitation, which will be handled by the Municipal Boy Scout Council and the Security Public Welfare Association. All funds will be deposited in the Central, China, Communications, China Farmers, and Hubei Provincial banks. As for the donations and items from citizens from all walks of life designated for慰勞 to the front-line generals and soldiers fighting against the bandits, the association will register them separately and transfer them to the front line. (6th)

Western Anhui Suffers from Severe Drought

No Major Rain for Three Months; Tens of Thousands of Disaster Victims Awaiting Relief

Bengbu Communication: The major products of western Anhui are bamboo, wood, tea, and hemp. The area has always been known as a rich and prosperous region. However, since the Red Bandits ravaged and disturbed the area for four years, the people have suffered惨罹 and the local vitality has been lost. After the Red Bandits were eradicated, it was hoped that the rural areas would be restored and the people would recover, but there was a severe drought last year and a spring famine this year. People were displaced and impoverished. Fortunately, there was a bumper harvest in the autumn of this year, and the rice market was active, giving farmers a chance to recover. Unexpectedly, since autumn, there has been little rainfall, and various places have suffered from severe drought again. The autumn harvest has been reduced, and grain prices have soared. Now that it is winter and the weather is dry and cold, the drought is severe and the disaster area is expanding. Since autumn and winter, more than three months have passed without major rain. The red land is fragmented and the fields are cracked. The disaster area extends to six or seven counties, with Liuhuang, Liu'an, and Huoqiu counties being the most severely affected, followed by Huoshan, Hefei, and Yuexi counties. Under the circumstances of prolonged drought and no rain, people are hoping for rain as if they were hoping for rainbows, and they are extremely eager. Tens of thousands of disaster victims are feeling a lack of food and are struggling on the verge of starvation. The degree of famine is almost the same as in the northern Anhui counties. Now that the winter is cold, the disaster victims are crying out for help and urgently need relief. All hope that the government will quickly release winter relief to救济 save the remaining survivors. (6th)

Guangdong Construction Department: Building Meteorological Stations in Various Places; Personnel Have Been Dispatched to Actively Prepare to Benefit Rural Water Conservancy

Guangzhou Communication: Liu Weichi, Director of the Construction Department, believes that rainfall measurement is of great importance to rural water conservancy construction. He has decided to implement the original plan and dispatch personnel to prepare for the construction of meteorological stations in five locations: Shantou, Haikou, Beihai, Maoming, and Sanya. He has also appointed Chen Tongji, Liao Shudu, and Zhang Yun, the head of the Guangzhou Shipai Meteorological Observatory, as preparation personnel, ordering them to be responsible for planning and opening. Director Chen has established a preparation office in the department. Director Liu has reported the situation to Provincial Government Chairman Huang for review and requested funds for handling. Chairman Huang has approved an allocation of 50,000 yuan for construction and start-up costs. The five meteorological stations will be planned and completed within a short period of time and construction will begin. In order to train personnel to handle meteorological affairs, the Planning Director has decided to hold a training class for meteorological personnel. Therefore, after the preparation office was established, it immediately began to handle the following matters: (1) purchasing machinery; (2) building new sites; (3) holding training classes. Director Liu also believes that the Guangzhou Meteorological Observatory has been established for three years. It was originally planned that the observatory would be the provincial meteorological headquarters, and the five meteorological stations in Shantou and other places would be the branch stations. However, due to funding issues in the past, the five meteorological stations have not been realized, so the province only has one meteorological station, with no distinction between headquarters and branches. It has now been decided that after the five meteorological stations are completed, the division can be carried out.

Kunshan

Clearing Overdue Land Tax

The county has a total of over 1,091,680 mu of cultivated land, with a land tax quota of over 1,162,670 yuan. However, due to successive years of poor harvests, the full amount has not been collected, resulting in a large accumulation of arrears. After exempting the arrears up to the 15th year, the accumulated arrears from the 16th to the 24th year amounted to over 858,831 yuan. Now, the county government, considering the people's financial capacity, has decided to clear and recover the arrears gradually over the years.

Changzhou

Rickshaw Permit Dispute

Rickshaw pullers operating at the train station in Wuyi County are required to have a small permit issued by the rickshaw companies. This permit costs five jiao (cents) of silver dollars per month and is not collected from the rickshaw pullers. Recently, the rickshaw companies suddenly violated this established practice and started charging each rickshaw puller an additional two fen (cents) per permit per day. As a result, the rickshaw pullers are unwilling to pay and have voluntarily returned their permits to the companies. As a result, none of the rickshaw pullers are operating at the station, causing great inconvenience for passengers arriving and departing. This situation has persisted for several days. The railway authorities telegraphed the Shanghai Railway Bureau and the party and government organs for instructions. The county party headquarters, in order to maintain current transportation, had committee member Wang Chao invite County Magistrate Hou Lizong and Public Security Bureau Chief Xu Baoguang to discuss solutions at the Farmers' Association on the 6th. The result was a notification to the rickshaw pullers' union to inform all rickshaw pullers to resume operations at the station without permits. The permit fee issue will be resolved at a party and government meeting. In addition, a telegram will be sent to the Shanghai Railway Bureau to cancel the small permits. Upon hearing the news, the rickshaw pullers resumed operations at the station that day, and transportation was restored.

Zhenjiang

Gradual Dredging of the Shajiang River

The Jiangsu Construction Department has proposed that the Huai River Diversion to the Sea Engineering Office implement the dredging of the Shajiang River, the New River, and the Chaimi River in two phases. The first phase involves the construction of embankments along the Shajiang River, the New River, and the Chaimi River, as well as partial straightening of the New River and the Chaimi River, requiring a total of 236,560 yuan. The second phase involves dredging the New River, the Chaimi River, and the Wanggong River, requiring a total of 250,006 yuan and 83 fen. The total cost for both phases is 486,766 yuan and 83 fen. Investigations show that the terrain in the area along the river is low-lying and has long been subject to flooding from the Yi and Mu Rivers, resulting in disasters nine out of ten years, causing extreme suffering for the people along the river, who are eagerly hoping for a solution. The first phase of the embankment construction project seems to be of urgent necessity, but the total cost still requires more than 230,000 yuan, which is difficult to raise. A special request has been submitted to the provincial government for approval. Chairman Chen submitted it to the provincial government meeting for discussion, and it was decided to postpone it until next year. The dredging of branch rivers and other projects that can be handled by the county will be guided by the Construction Department to the county government, which will handle them according to the labor service method.

Completion of Earthwork on the Nanping Section

The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway's Nanping section is being constructed at an accelerated pace. All earthwork was completed at the beginning of this month. It has now been decided to urge the engineering office to speed up the work in order to complete the opening to traffic as soon as possible and connect with the Guangdong-Hankou Railway to handle joint transportation.

A Notorious Bandit in Eastern Zhejiang Was Killed

Chen Guangming, a Red bandit from Zhejiang Province, is 25 years old and a native of Yongkang. In the past, he gathered bandits in his hometown to kidnap and extort, committing numerous crimes. He was once arrested and detained in a detention center, but he escaped and joined the bandit leader Wang Daying's command, serving as a supervisor on the military commission. In Yongkang, Jinyun, Dongyang, Xianju, and other counties, he kidnapped and extorted ransoms, and shot and killed dozens of civilians. This summer, he fled to Shanghai to evade pursuit. He was arrested by the Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters and escorted to the Yongkang County Government in Zhejiang. During the recognition, he escaped from the car. Later, he was discovered in a dilapidated temple here. During the transfer to Yiwu, he tried to escape again and was shot and killed on the spot by the escorting police.

Huzhou

Four Ships Robbed by Bandits

The four overnight ships from this city to Xiaoshe, Shengji and Yuji, and to Xiaoxikou, Gongji and Mao Bao, departed from Huzhou simultaneously on the afternoon of the 4th. While passing through Musanting in Changxing County late at night, a bandit ship suddenly appeared. Over a dozen bandits, armed with wooden-case guns and rapid-firing guns, shouted in mixed accents and fired a shot into the air, ordering the ships to stop. The bandits immediately searched each ship. After the robbery, the bandits sped away in their original ship. On the Shengji ship, a passenger from Xiaofeng lost a wooden box containing galoshes, sneakers, scarves, and other items, worth over 100 yuan. A passenger named Bai on the Jinji ship had 53 yuan in silver dollars, three boxes of kerosene, and four baskets of salt stolen. The Gongji ship lost goods worth over 20 yuan. The Mao Bao ship had 80 yuan in legal tender stolen, as well as pawn tickets redeemed on behalf of villagers. The total loss of the four ships was estimated at several thousand yuan.

Yao Jinji Silk Factory's Carelessness

The Yao Jinji Electric Silk Weaving Factory, located at No. 46 Shuzhuangtai, North Gate of this city, caught fire accidentally at 3:40 AM on the 4th. After receiving the alarm, the Yilong firefighters from each district rushed to put out the fire. It took an hour to extinguish the fire. Seven ordinary houses, seven motors, and machine-woven silk fabrics were destroyed, with losses estimated at around 5,000 yuan. When the fire broke out, all the weavers escaped from the workshop, but two workers re-entered to retrieve their own clothes. At that time, the room was filled with thick smoke and flames, so there was no way to escape, and they died in the fire. The deceased were Tang Arong, 43 years old, from Danyang, and Fei Ahu, 23 years old, from Houzhuang, Wuxing.

A Minor Dispute Led to a Murder Case

The Zhentaixing South Goods Store on the east side of the Xishitang Bridge in Wangdian Town, Jiaxing, is owned by the town gentry Jiang Hengfu. On the 4th, the district court was notified to conduct an autopsy. The results showed that the deceased had a blunt force injury to his left waist, and both his left bladder and chest had signs of blunt force trauma, confirming that he died from his injuries. The murderer, Jiang Zhangsheng, was handed over to the court for detention and interrogation at 4 PM on the 4th. In addition, in the city, in front of the Li Xinpu Tobacco Shop at the southern end of the North Banqiao of the Grand Bridge, his wife, Zhou, helped him run the business. Zhou cried out for help, and neighbors rushed over upon hearing her cries, snatched the knife away, and rescued Zhou. Education News

Ministry of Railways Revises Rules for Selecting Students for Overseas Study

The Ministry of Railways has slightly revised the rules for selecting students for overseas study. The revisions are as follows: Article 5, item B, is revised as follows: "Those who have a university degree and have served in the ministry for more than one year and have excellent performance." Article 7, under items 1 and 2, a new item 3 is added. The article reads: "3. Those who have one of the qualifications in items A and B of Article 5 of these rules, the selection procedure may also use examination methods when necessary. The examination subjects and the number of admissions will be determined temporarily." The original item 3 of the rules is changed to item 4. Articles 8 and 9 are deleted, and the remaining articles are renumbered accordingly. Article 15 is revised as follows: "The tuition fees for students studying abroad under items 1, 2, and 3 of Article 7 will be paid from the month of arrival in the study abroad country. The allowance for students studying abroad under item 4 of Article 7 will be paid from the month of approval by the ministry. If they graduate and return to the country, the tuition fee will be issued up to the month of departure." Article 21 is revised as follows: "Students studying abroad under items 1, 2, and 3 of Article 7 must limit their study or research subjects to the scope of transportation science. They must fill out a voluntary application form stating their chosen country and subject, and it must be approved by the ministry. Once determined, it cannot be changed arbitrarily. If there is a need to change the subject due to actual circumstances, it should be submitted to the ministry for approval. Violators will have their tuition fees suspended. When there is a need for talent in a certain discipline, or when there are few students studying in a certain country, the ministry may, depending on the circumstances, designate them separately." Article 22 is revised as follows: "Students studying abroad on public funds must enter a school recognized by the ministry."

Ministry of Education Rewards and Encourages Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui Students to Pursue Further Studies

Allocating Special Funds from Border Education Funds, Formulating Methods, and Issuing Special Notices to All Universities

In order to reward and encourage Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students of all ethnic groups to pursue further studies in the interior, the Ministry of Education has recently issued a special order to all colleges and universities across the country, stating: "In order to reward and encourage Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students of all ethnic groups to pursue further studies in colleges and universities in the interior, starting this year, special funds will be allocated from the border education subsidy funds to provide subsidies. The outline of the measures for subsidizing Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students to pursue further studies in colleges and universities in the interior is now formulated. In addition to the announcement, the outline of the measures is hereby issued for your information." The outline of the measures is as follows:

(1) In order to reward and encourage Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students to pursue further studies in colleges and universities in the interior and to seek advanced studies, starting from the 25th year, a certain amount will be earmarked from the border education subsidy funds to serve as subsidies. (2) The number of subsidies is set at fifteen. Those who are admitted to public and registered colleges and universities may request subsidies. Those who are already studying at public or registered private colleges and universities may also apply for subsidies as a precedent. (3) The Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students who request subsidies are limited to those from the Mongolian, Tibetan, and Xinjiang provinces. (4) Those who request subsidies must provide the following procedures: A. Proof of documents from the local administrative organs, B. Proof of documents from the school admitted to, C. Graduation certificate or certificate from the original graduated middle school, D. Three recent 4-inch half-length photos. The above documents, together with the application form, shall be submitted to the Ministry of Education for verification and processing. (5) Students who are approved for subsidies will receive a subsidy of 300 yuan per person per year, which will be allocated by the Ministry of Education to the school where the student is enrolled on a monthly basis for distribution to the student. (6) Students receiving subsidies must abide by school rules and work hard in their studies. If they violate school rules and are subject to school disciplinary action, or if they neglect their studies and fail more than three subjects, the Ministry of Education may, depending on the circumstances, reduce, suspend, or recover the subsidy. (7) All public or registered private colleges and universities that have Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students receiving subsidies under this outline shall report the student's conduct and academic performance to the Ministry of Education at the end of each academic year for assessment. (8) Those who impersonate Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students, or impersonate their names, and forge proof of documents, will be subject to a corresponding penalty in addition to the recovery of the subsidy if discovered. (9) Those who have received subsidies from administrative organs at all levels and those who have public-funded treatment from specialized schools may not apply for subsidies. (10) This outline may be revised by the Ministry of Education when necessary.

Our Supervising Office for Students Studying in Japan Takes Action to Stop Students from Skipping Grades; Liu Zhong Forges a Certificate and Is Sent Back to China

(Central News Agency, Tokyo) Chen Juepu, the supervisor of Chinese students studying in Japan, has been actively rectifying the affairs of students studying in Japan since taking office, making every effort to do so. Those who seek to skip grades by improper means are strictly punished. Recently, Liu Zhong, a student from Yexian County, forged a graduation certificate from the Chaoyang Ning College in Beiping and requested registration and introduction from the office. After investigation, he was reported to the Ministry of Education for sending him back to China. Afterwards, in order to warn students studying in the East, Supervisor Chen issued a notice to serve as a warning for the future. The original text of the notice is as follows: "Since the beginning of my tenure, I have declared the policy of upholding morals, encouraging learning, and rectifying discipline, hoping that students studying in the East will encourage each other to cultivate profound knowledge, noble character, and a spirit of perseverance in order to achieve the goal of serving the country and gaining a reputation overseas. I have also visited the Japanese authorities and related universities to unify the introduction and eliminate the malpractices of improper admission. The fifth notice of November 28 last year used extremely painful words to admonish students studying in the East to cherish themselves and not damage the reputation of the whole body for their own convenience. Otherwise, they will be severely sanctioned in accordance with the orders of the Ministry. All students studying in the East should be able to recall that in the past year, most of the Japanese related schools, except for one or two schools that seem to have not yet understood the policy of this office, have tightened their management of students studying abroad. Those who are expelled for misconduct or excessive absenteeism have also been reported from time to time. This supervisor is both happy and worried, and is planning to work together to improve and seek the improvement of the academic atmosphere. However, recently, Liu Zhong, a student from Yexian County, came to the office to present a graduation certificate from the Chaoyang College in Beiping for registration and introduction. Although the content of the certificate, including the Ministry's seal, the school's seal, and the impression, are all available and lifelike, upon closer inspection of the student's language and demeanor, there are doubts. After consulting the Chaoyang College, it was confirmed that it was a forgery. The case was then reported to the Ministry of Education for verification. On November 3, we received an order stating that all the presented documents were understood. The student Liu Zhong forged a graduation certificate and official seals, violating criminal law. The office was ordered to find a way to order the student to return to China for investigation in accordance with the law, and the forged certificate was stored in the Ministry for cancellation. According to this order, officials were dispatched from the office on the 20th of this month at 9:00 to escort the student to Yokohama to take the Rokko Maru back to China, and a letter was sent to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau to transfer him to the Ministry of Education for investigation. Since the revolution in our country, everything has been waiting to be done, and the most lacking is talented and knowledgeable people. The cultivation of talented people depends entirely on gradual progress year by year. There is no possibility of skipping grades and achieving success in one fell swoop. Although the reasons for students holding forged certificates to request registration and introduction from the office are different, they are all trying to obtain graduation qualifications from Japanese schools by deceptive means and compete with those who have worked hard for years to obtain the same status after returning to the country. However, this is really too extravagant. How can the way of learning allow skipping grades? Why do the education systems of various countries in the East and West specify the time limit and system? Elementary and middle school students can also take any titles and positions. This is the first reason why it is impossible. Furthermore, the certificate presented by the student concerns his personal academic achievements and the reputation of the country. If the authenticity is not distinguished and good and bad are mixed, who in the country will be willing to work hard? The resulting malpractice will inevitably lead to a competition for falsehood, making the country's education, culture, and social order unbearable to ask, and the country's reputation and international credibility will also be swept away. This is the second reason why it is impossible. Recently, there have been many criticisms of the academic achievements of students studying in Japan from the United States. The reason is that a few students know how to be opportunistic and do not value practicality, resulting in a decline in the value of all students. On the other hand, the so-called domestic schoolwork is booming, but the name does not match the reality, and it is despised by others, making the domestic education level suffer from criticism. This is the third reason why it is impossible. At a time when the country is striving for construction, eliminating falsehood and advocating practicality is an important creed of the New Life Movement. How can students studying abroad be unaware of this? Now, or just arrived in the neighboring country, they disregard the country's laws and regulations. Even if they are lucky enough to be admitted, they deceive teachers and friends, deceive the country and society, and deceiving others is deceiving themselves. Their minds are not worthy of asking. In the future, when they return to the country to serve, they have no strength to deal with it. If they don't shirk responsibility, they will be perfunctory, or even delay national affairs, ruin their lives, harm others, and eventually harm themselves. The relationship between public and private is even greater. This is the fourth reason why it is impossible. Confucius said, 'If the name is not correct, the words will not be smooth.' It is said that 'the name is only a tool, and it cannot be used by a false person.' The certificate is a tool with official seals, school seals, and registration of subjects, levels, and titles of the country and society. Can it be forged, stolen, and used at will? Is it different from sitting idly by while villains and traitors steal people's property, disrupt the country's politics, and fail to stop them? This supervisor loves the country more than his life, and loves the students as his children. His duties are to not be perfunctory and evasive, to not nitpick, but to not condone evil. Ma Su was beheaded and the three armies obeyed. Zhuang Jia was executed and the Qi army was disciplined. A viper stings the hand, and a hero cuts off his wrist. Take the benefit of its weight and choose the light of its harm. National law and private feelings are difficult to balance. There is a definite conclusion about merits and demerits. In short, all the gains and losses that concern the country and the students' future are done with all my heart and effort, and I will not hesitate to work hard or complain. Now that Liu Zhong has left, it is impossible to recover. I hope that the students studying in the East will take this as a warning, persuade each other, advocate practical learning, and not let this unfortunate thing happen again and again. You must know that our future loyalty and bravery to serve the country is based on the current self-improvement. If you are ignorant of the gains and losses, take advantage of the moment, and hope that you can deceive and take false names, you will damage the reputation of all students studying in the East and cause endless worries for the country. Not only will the national laws and regulations not forgive you, but also the academic circles at home and abroad will abandon you. I hope you will encourage each other." The notification is issued for public knowledge on November 25th, 25th year of the Republic of China, Supervisor Chen Chipu.

Overview of Educational Expenditure in Zhejiang Province in the Last Eight Years

A Definite Standard Was Established Starting in the 22nd Year

Educational expenditure in Zhejiang Province can be divided into two categories: business expenditure under the jurisdiction of the Department of Education and business expenditure not under the jurisdiction of the Department of Education. The former is compiled by the Department of Education into a general budget for each year's revenue and expenditure and sent to the Department of Finance for compilation into the provincial local revenue and expenditure budget book, which is submitted to the provincial government meeting for approval and then submitted to the central government for approval. The provincial treasury allocates funds according to the amount. Since the establishment of the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education, the amount of business expenditure under the jurisdiction of the Department of Education in the most recent eight years has increased or decreased with the prosperity or shortage of the provincial treasury, which has greatly affected the advancement of educational undertakings. In November of the 22nd year, the Department of Education and the Department of Finance jointly discussed and formulated 11 articles of the Zhejiang Provincial Educational Expenditure and other funds management and payment methods, which were submitted to the provincial government meeting for discussion and promulgation and reported to the Executive Yuan for record. Since then, educational expenditure has had a definite guarantee and has not been drastically reduced as in the three years from the 21st year onwards. The budget amount for the provincial educational expenditure in the province's most recent eight years from the 18th year to the 25th year is recorded below: (1) 2,392,173 yuan in the 18th year, (2) 2,636,951 yuan in the 19th year, (3) 2,839,238 yuan in the 20th year, (4) 2,273,025 yuan in the 21st year, (5) 2,106,436 yuan in the 22nd year, (6) 2,275,958 yuan in the 23rd year, (7) 2,380,844 yuan in the 24th year, (8) 2,835,337 yuan in the 25th year.

Mathematics Discussion Group of the Secondary School Advancement Association

A total of eight important issues were discussed, and each school was requested to study and report separately

The Shanghai Secondary School Advancement Association held a mathematics discussion group last week at the YMCA in Baixianqiao. A total of eight issues were discussed. The proceedings of the meeting have been compiled and published as follows:

Attendees: Zheng Xigu, Zhang Zhonghuan, Zhu Fenghao, Ju Bingyao, Hua Zhiwen, Liu Suisheng, Hua Zheng, and Peng Shuhua from the Provincial Shanghai High School; He Shihao and Yao Wenxun from Wusong Middle School; Xia Bochu, Wang Shuaizhu, and Wu Shangqian from McLaren Middle School; Wang Hanzhong, Zhang Yuanshu, and Ding Rukang from Daxia Affiliated High School; Chen Yusheng and Wu Youxiao from Chengzhong Middle School; Shi Qiming, Qian Dong, and Yao Yue from Guangshi Middle School; Wu Zhuoyun and Huang Ding from Nanyang Middle School; Wang Rui from Sishang Middle School; Xu Anren from Qiaoguang Middle School; Wang Guyu from Kaiming Middle School; Chen Lianshi and Cao Chouyu from Fudan Affiliated High School; Chen Huanwen and Cao Mulan from the Chinese Vocational School; Xi Lunchao from Guangxia Middle School; Wang Zhaoqi from Shanghai Preschool Normal School; Wang Bingtai from Private Shanghai High School; Dai Tiejun and Shen Xiaochu from Qingcai Middle School; Chen Dezhen, Qin Mei, and Ding Liangying from McTyeire School; Zuo Jingqi from Xinhuan Vocational School; Jin Pin and Zheng Xigu from Guanghua Affiliated High School. After reporting, Zhu Fenghao from the Provincial Shanghai High School was elected as chairman, and Zhang Zhongshi as secretary.

Issues for Discussion: (1) How should the mathematics curriculum in secondary schools be designed to connect with universities? Conclusion: A. Investigate university entrance exam questions; B. Investigate textbooks from various secondary schools; C. Study connection methods. (2) How to increase students' interest in mathematics? Conclusion: A. Teaching materials should be practical; B. Pay attention to student practice; C. Eliminate students' fear; D. Avoid excessively heavy workload; E. Pay attention to teachers' teaching methods. (3) How to increase students' learning efficiency? Conclusion: A. Physical exertion should not be forced, but psychological exertion should be encouraged; B. Present teaching objectives; C. Pay attention to calculation methods; D. Pay attention to applied examples; E. Hold more exams. (4) How to help students who are lagging behind? Conclusion: A. Extra tutoring; B. Instructors should provide guidance at all times. (5) How to increase supplementary reading materials for high-achieving students? Conclusion: A. Supplementary materials should be abundant; B. Increase practice without increasing learning materials. (6) How should blackboard exercises be implemented? Conclusion: A. Have students practice first, then do blackboard exercises; B. Add more blackboards. (7) How to solve the problem of grading exercise books? Conclusion: A. Exercise books should be divided into two categories: those to be submitted and those for self-use; B. Set a specific time for practice; C. Prevent malpractices; D. Emphasize self-study guidance; E. Exercise books should be spot-checked in batches, but all must be reviewed; F. Encourage students to correct their own work; G. Loose-leaf exercise books are more convenient. (8) How should mathematics teachers improve themselves? Conclusion: A. Improve training courses; B. Organize research groups.

Separate Research: After the discussion, it was unanimously decided that all eight discussion issues should be sent to each member school for separate research, and the association should be informed in writing. The information will then be compiled and published. After receiving these discussion topics, each school must identify one topic, conduct research, and submit a written report within the semester. The association is also scheduled to hold its 58th general meeting at the YMCA in Baixianqiao at 12:00 noon on the 19th of this month. Notices will be sent out soon.

China Youth Basketball Registration Begins Today

Still Divided into Four Divisions, Deadline on the 19th

The basketball tournament organized by the Shanghai YMCA every year (the 7th edition this year) will continue to be held. Le Xiurong, Zhou Jiaqi, Wang Ruisheng, Li Feiyun, and Cao Tingzan have been appointed as committee members. The regulations have been slightly revised, with the aim of giving each team the opportunity to compete. Therefore, only teams that have not participated in other league competitions of other basketball associations, such as the Sports Advancement Association, the Municipal Association, and the Western Youth Association, are eligible to participate. This year, the tournament is still divided into four divisions: school, commercial, bank, and women's. If there are too many teams in each division, they will be further divided into groups. However, divisions with fewer than four teams will not be held. The competition method will be a single round-robin system. For the award method, the champion team of each division will be awarded a silk banner by the association. If there are more than ten teams in each division, an additional award will be given to the runner-up, and each team member will receive a medal. Registration starts today and ends on the 19th. Each men's team is limited to ten players, and each women's team is limited to fourteen players. Each team must submit a full team photo. Copies of the regulations are available upon request. Those who wish to join can obtain them from the association's office at the Sichuan Road branch.

University Sports Federation To Hold Cross-Country Race Today, Starts at 3:00 PM in Front of Guanghua School Gate, A Total of Five Universities Participating in the 3.5-Mile Race

Since the Jiangnan University Sports Association was reorganized into the Shanghai University Sports Federation, all work has followed the old rules. The first cross-country race was originally scheduled for the 5th, but due to incomplete planning, it was changed to today (the 8th) at 3:00 PM. The race will start in front of the Guanghua University gate on Da Xi Road. The total distance is 3 and a half miles (i.e., 3.5 miles). Five schools have registered to participate, including Fudan, Jinan, Chizhi, Tongji, and Guanghua. Each school is limited to ten registrants. The scoring quota is limited to the top six finishers from each school, calculated using the inverse method, i.e., the first place gets one point, the second place gets two points, and so on. The team with the fewest total points wins the championship. The competition will be held as scheduled, rain or shine. In the last edition (i.e., the last edition during the Jiangnan University era, held in Zhenru), the championship was won by the Fudan team, and the individual champion was from Jinan. This year, Fudan still has the most even strength, so the hopes are still high. The race numbers have not yet been assigned because the team rosters have not yet been submitted completely. They will be assigned temporarily today. The route and the rosters that have been submitted are listed below:

Route

From the Guanghua school gate, head west, passing through Zhongshan Road, Da Xi Road, Fales Road, Hongqiao Road, Bilan Road, Lincoln Road, then return to Da Xi Road, turn to Zhongshan Road, and return to the starting point. The total distance is 2 and a half miles.

Local News

Over a Thousand People in Mourning: Duan's Remains Depart Yesterday Afternoon with Utmost Honor; Traffic Interrupted on Roads Along the Procession Route; Special Train Left Shanghai in the Afternoon, Passing Through Beijing and Transported to Beiping; National Funeral to be Held on a Selected Date After Arriving in Beiping on the 10th

The remains of the late former Provisional Chief Executive Duan Qirui departed yesterday at 12:00 noon. A special train transported them to Beiping at 5:00 PM, and a national funeral will be held on a selected date. Details are as follows:

Departure at Noon

The remains departed at 12:00 noon, proceeding from Avenue Joffre, through Rue Mentiigny, Yu Qiaqing Road, Beijing Road, Zhejiang Road, Boundary Road, and arriving at the North Railway Station. The procession consisted of: (1) 16 mounted police; (2) a military band; (3) a memorial pavilion; (4) an honor guard; (5) a color pavilion; (6) 240 monks and Taoists; (7) a military band; (8) a spirit tablet sedan; (9) guests in mourning; (10) pallbearers; (11) a group of filial sons; (12) the hearse; (13) the bereaved family. The procession extended for more than two li. The authorities of the Public Concession and the French Concession, in addition to dispatching a large number of police to maintain order and protect the route, also sent foreign police and the Shanghai Volunteer Corps to escort the procession. Traffic was interrupted on all roads along the procession route, and passing vehicles had to take detours. The crowds standing on both sides of the road to watch were extremely dense, truly an unprecedented scene.

Pallbearers

Those participating as pallbearers yesterday included Chairman Lin of the National Government, Premier Jiang of the Executive Yuan represented by Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Garrison Commander of Songhu Yang Hu, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau Cai Jingjun, Legislative Member Zheng Hongnian, President of the Military Council Chen Diaoyuan, Minister to Turkey He Yaozu, Superintendent of the Donghai Customs Zhou Xiuwen, Qian Xinzhi, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Gong Xianzhou, Ye Gongchuo, Huang Yanpei from the local associations, and all staff members of the funeral committee, as well as relatives and friends of the Duan family, totaling more than a thousand people.

A Glimpse of the North Station

At 2:00 PM, the remains passed through Yu Qiaqing Road. Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Qian Xinzhi, and others held a public memorial service at the Da Zhonghua Hotel at the intersection of Fuzhou Road. They then paid respects at the roadside in front of the Xiaoyao Ballroom at the intersection of Nanjing Road. The procession arrived at the North Railway Station at 2:40 PM. At that time, the area around the North Station was guarded by more than 500 security personnel and police, and traffic was blocked. When the remains entered the East Station gate through the memorial archway on Boundary Road, all military police raised their guns in salute to the rhythm of the military music. The atmosphere was very solemn.

Departure of the Funeral Train

The funeral train was parked on the old Songhu platform. The other vehicles were parked on platforms 3 and 4. After the remains arrived on the platform, a portrait was set up, and a public memorial service was held. The pallbearers and those in mourning, led by Mayor Wu, paid their respects and bowed before the remains. Directors Huang Boqiao of the two railway bureaus and members of the administration of the two railway bureaus also participated. At this time, it was already raining, and guests arriving to pay their respects continued to arrive. It wasn't until around 4:00 PM that the service ended. The funeral train departed north at 5:00 PM amidst the sound of military music. It is scheduled to arrive in Beijing at 8:00 AM this morning. After being paid tribute by the National Government and ministers of various departments, the train will cross the river, depart north from Pukou at 1:30 PM in the afternoon, and arrive at Qianmen in Beiping on the morning of the 10th. The remains will then be transported from Qianmen to the Wohfo Temple in the Western Hills for temporary storage, and a national funeral will be held on a selected date.

Train Composition

The funeral and mourning train consisted of 18 cars, combined from the Shanghai-Nanjing, Tianjin-Pukou, Pinghan, and Beiping-Liaoning lines. The facilities were complete. The order was as follows: (1) Locomotive; (2) 1211 Tianjin-Pukou Third Class; (3) 1203 Tianjin-Pukou Third Class; (4) 251 Beiping-Liaoning Second Class; (5) 2058 Tianjin-Pukou Dining Car; (6) 607 Tianjin-Pukou First Class Sleeper; (7) 202 Shanghai-Nanjing First Class Sleeper; (8) 324 Beiping-Liaoning First Class Sleeper; (9) Hearse; (10) 209 Tianjin-Pukou Lounge Car; (11) 201 Shanghai-Nanjing First Class Sleeper; (12) 814 Tianjin-Pukou Second Class Sleeper; (13) 044 Beiping-Liaoning Second Class Sleeper; (14) 620 Shanghai-Nanjing Second Class Guard Car; (15) 662 Shanghai-Nanjing Third Class Car; (16) 132 Beiping-Liaoning Third Class Car; (17) 982 Shanghai-Nanjing Guard Car; (18) 6669 Baggage Car.

Those Accompanying the Remains

The train consisted of eighteen cars, composed of vehicles from the Shanghai-Nanjing, Tianjin-Pukou, Pinghan, and Beiping-Liaoning Railways. The equipment was complete. Accompanying the remains were Deng Zanqing, Cao Jiezhi, Zhang Xiaolin, Gong Xianzhou, Gong Zhenzhou, Tang Boping, Gu Shiru, Huang Yanpei, and Donghai Customs Superintendent Zhou Xiuwen, totaling more than one hundred people, traveling in two first-class sleeper cars. The remaining cars were one first-class sleeper car for the bereaved family and one first-class sleeper car for the filial sons. All accompanying staff traveled in second and third-class cars. Song Zheyuan, chairman of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, and his representative Men Zhizhong, as well as former Premier Jin Yunpeng, who came to welcome the remains, had taken the Shanghai-Beiping through train on the evening of the 6th to report to Tianjin and Beiping and prepare for the arrival of the remains.

Arrival in Beiping the Day After Tomorrow

The special train is scheduled to pass through Beijing today. It will make brief stops at each port along the way for roadside memorial services. The train schedule is as follows: Depart Shanghai North Station at 5:00 PM on December 7th, arrive at Kunshan at 6:08 PM, depart at 6:30 PM, arrive at Suzhou at 7:30 PM, depart at 8:00 PM, arrive at Wuxi at 9:05 PM, depart at 9:25 PM, arrive at Changzhou at 10:15 PM, depart at 10:46 PM, arrive at Danyang at 11:49 PM, depart at 12 minutes past midnight on the 8th, arrive at Zhenjiang West Station at 95 minutes past midnight, depart at 1:30 AM, arrive at Nanjing at 8:00 AM, depart from Pukou at 1:30 PM, arrive at Bengbu at 6:49 PM, depart at 7:09 PM, arrive at Xuzhou at 11:14 PM, depart at 11:44 PM, arrive at Jinan at 9:12 AM on the 9th, depart at 10:12 AM, arrive at Tianjin Central Station at 6:45 PM.

Kong Xiangxi Is Recovering

Resumed Office at the Central Bank Yesterday

Kong Xiangxi, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, had previously suffered from a cold, and his old illness had recurred. After recuperation, he has recovered and resumed office at the Central Bank yesterday. However, to avoid the jolting of the train, he will not enter Beijing for the time being.

Foreign Minister Zhang Returns to Beijing Yesterday

Foreign Minister Zhang Qun, along with Secretary Duan Maolan, arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing on the morning of the 5th to attend the public memorial for former Head of State Duan Qirui. Initially planning to stay overnight in Shanghai and then return to Nanjing, he extended his stay by one day to assist with the funeral arrangements for Huang Fu. He departed from Shanghai on the 12:00 midnight express train last night to return to Nanjing. Railway Minister Zhang Jia'ao, Vice Minister Zeng Rongfu, and Guangzhou Mayor Zeng Yangfu, however, took the 11:00 midnight express train to Nanjing.

I am deeply grateful for your active fundraising to慰勞 the officers and soldiers in Suiyuan who are suppressing the bandits.
