China-Foreign Cultural Association Holds Farewell Reception for Ambassador Wang Zhengting and Farewell Luncheon for Gao Leibo, Director of French Education

The China-Foreign Cultural Association of this city held a tea party at the International Hotel at 5:00 PM yesterday to bid farewell to our newly appointed Ambassador to the United States, Wang Zhengting, and Gao Leibo, Director of Education of the French Municipal Council. Chairman Chu Minyi presided, and Wang and Gao both stood up to express their thanks. Details are as follows:

Guests Attending Yesterday Evening The guests attending last night included Ambassador Wang, Gao Leibo, Wang Chonghui, Chu Minyi, Wei Daoming, Li Shizeng, Liu Yunfang, Xiao Jinfang, Zhu Changnian, Zhao Jinqing, Qu Wenliu, Wang Yiting, Wu Kaisheng, Guo Bingwen, Dai Baoxun, Tai Shuangqiu, Chu Huiseng, He Zhenya, Su Xin, Commercial Counselor of the French Embassy, French Vice Consul Blionfan, Deputy Principal of the Sino-French Institute Xi Peide, and over a hundred others.

Chairman's Speech Chairman Chu Minyi delivered a farewell speech, stating that culture is the soul of a nation. With increasingly close international relations, it is necessary to study each other and give full play to the cultures of various countries in order to promote and enhance them, striving for the unification of world culture and working for international peace. Ambassador Wang has always been extremely dedicated to cultural endeavors. In addition to diplomatic negotiations, it is hoped that he will also strive for Sino-American cultural exchange. Gao Leibo has been engaged in education in China for many years. Although their missions are different as they return to their respective countries today, their common goal is to promote culture. I extend my best wishes to them.

Mr. Wang's Reply Subsequently, Ambassador Wang stood up to express his thanks, stating that he deeply sympathized with the points made. Countries in the East and West have their own cultures. Similarities should be used to facilitate communication, and differences should also be addressed. In the 20th century, transportation is convenient, and learning foreign languages is a tool for transporting culture. European and American universities now have departments of Eastern Studies, but this is still not enough. The China-Foreign Cultural Association's efforts in exchanging culture are deeply appreciated. I wish the association progress and success. Finally, Gao Leibo replied with thanks, and a photograph was taken. The gathering concluded in a happy atmosphere at around 6:00 PM.

Huang Fu's Body Moved to Funeral Parlor Yesterday, Encoffining Held This Afternoon, President Yu and the American Ambassador and Others Paid Their Respects Yesterday, Chairman Lin, President Jiang, and Others Sent Telegrams of Condolence, Burial Site to be Selected at Moganshan, Memorial Service and Funeral Date Undetermined

After the death of National Government Committee member Huang Fu at his residence the day before yesterday, his body was moved to the Chinese Funeral Parlor on Haig Road at 3:00 PM yesterday. The encoffining is scheduled for 3:00 PM this afternoon. Chairman Lin, President Cai, and others have sent telegrams of condolence. Many people paid their respects yesterday. Details are as follows:

Moving to the Funeral Parlor

Huang's body was originally scheduled to be moved to the funeral parlor at 10:00 AM yesterday. However, the Huang family, following Buddhist customs, believed that the body should not be moved while it was still warm. Therefore, it was delayed until 3:00 PM in the afternoon, when a hearse was sent by the funeral parlor to take the body to the Number One Funeral Room. Technicians then performed embalming. No ceremony was held at the time. Only Madam Shen Jingying, Huang's wife, and his daughters, along with Foreign Minister Zhang Qun, Zhejiang Civil Affairs Director Xu Qingfu (who arrived yesterday), Financial Affairs Director Cheng Yuanfan, former Vice Minister Xu Xiuzhi, former Mayor of Beiping Yuan Liang, his relative Shen Yi, Director of the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, Huang Boqiao, Director of the Two Roads Bureau, and former subordinates Ge Jingyou, Ge Jingen, Zhao Shuyong, and others, followed to express their condolences and arrange everything. A spirit hall was set up in the main hall, with Huang's portrait placed on the altar, along with incense candles and offerings. The main entrance of the funeral parlor was decorated with plain-colored streamers.

Encoffining This Afternoon

The funeral parlor will send staff to guard the hall overnight. The encoffining will be held at 3:00 PM this afternoon. At that time, representatives from the party and government, as well as Chinese and foreign friends of Huang Fu during his lifetime, will attend the ceremony. According to Huang's relative, Shen Yi, Mr. Huang left instructions to his family before his death that the funeral should be kept simple and should not be Westernized. Therefore, the burial clothes, coffin, and all ceremonies should follow ancient customs. Mr. Huang liked to live in Moganshan during his lifetime and founded Mogan Primary School and other endeavors. To fulfill his last wishes, it is planned to be buried at the foot of Moganshan in the future. The date of the memorial service and burial has not yet been determined. It is not known whether the government will offer any preferential treatment, but the timeline will not be long, so that Mr. Huang's soul can rest in peace.

Yesterday's Mourners

After learning of Huang's death, Wang Jingwei, Chairman of the Central Political Council, who is in England, immediately telegraphed to send Central Committee member Chu Minyi to Huang's residence yesterday morning to express condolences and present a wreath. In addition, those who went to Huang's residence and funeral parlor yesterday to express their condolences included President of the Control Yuan Yu Youren, Central Committee member Zhang Jingjiang, Xue Dubi, representative of Deputy Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission Feng Yuxiang, Zou Lu, member of the Central Standing Committee (on behalf of Madam Zhao Shujia), Li Liejun, member of the Central Committee (on behalf of Tao Zhongyao), Guangzhou Mayor Hui Yangfu, Shanghai Public Security Bureau Chief Cai Jinjun, Zhou Jue, Director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Office in Shanghai, Chen Juesheng, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau (on behalf of Zhao Weiru), Zhou Yongneng, counselor of the Municipal Government of Shanghai, Tang Youren and his brothers Tang Xuanwei and Tang Bonian, former Vice Minister, as well as Huang Yanpei, Jiang Wenyu, Yang Weiyu, Zhang Yonghong, Fan Shisheng, U.S. Ambassador to China Mr. and Mrs. Johnson, Consul General Gao Qi and his wife, Kita, military attache of the Japanese Embassy in Shanghai, and over a hundred of Huang's Japanese friends, including Shincheng Shincang, Ueno Taichu, and Inoue. In addition, Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng sent Geng Jiaji, secretary of the Municipal Government, to Huang's residence to assist with the funeral arrangements.

Chairman Lin's Telegram

After Huang's death, Mayor Wu, Foreign Minister Zhang, and Mrs. Huang telegraphed Chairman Lin, President Jiang, and others to report the news. Mrs. Huang received a telegram of condolence from Chairman Lin yesterday, which read: "I was shocked and saddened to learn of Mr. Yingbai's death in Shanghai on the 6th. Mr. Huang was a pillar of the party and the country, a mentor to the people, with profound knowledge of both Chinese and Western cultures, and talent in both civil and military affairs. He went to Shanghai for medical treatment for liver disease, and I had hoped that he would recover and continue his great contributions. His sudden death is a cause of grief for all those with insight. I believe that Mr. Huang's contributions to the country will be admired by all, and his great plans and strategies will be a model for the future. I hope you will restrain your grief and assist in major affairs to comfort his spirit. Lin Sen, seal."

President Jiang's Telegram

Chairman Jiang sent a telegram of condolence from Huaqing Pool, which read: "I am deeply saddened by the death of my second brother (note: Huang and Jiang had a sworn brotherhood). I hope you will restrain your grief and not be too saddened. Zhongzheng bows." Minister of Military Affairs He Yingqin, Chairman of the Fujian Provincial Government Chen Yi, newly appointed Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government Zhu Jiahua, Nanjing Mayor Ma Chaojun, Madam Chen Shuying, wife of President of the Legislative Yuan Sun Ke, Li Sihao, Chairman of the Economic Committee of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, Ambassador to the Netherlands Jin Wensi, newly appointed Ambassador to Denmark Wei Duozu, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau Chen Juesheng, Gao Zongwu, Director of the Asian Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Jiang Menglin, President of Peking University, Tang Erhe, He Qigong, Yin Tong, and Huang's Japanese friends Uchida Fukuji, Ishikawa Jun, and Western friend Ferguson, also sent dozens of telegrams of condolence.

Central Executive and Supervisory Committees' Telegram

The Central Executive and Supervisory Committees sent a telegram to Huang Fu's family on the 7th, which read: "We salute the family of Mr. Huang Yingbai. Mr. Huang Yingbai was an elder statesman who worked tirelessly and devotedly. We had hoped that he would recover his health soon and work together to overcome difficulties. His sudden death is a cause of deep grief. We hereby send our condolences. We hope you will accept the changes and restrain your grief to attend to important matters. What we look forward to. The Central Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Chinese Kuomintang, seal." Yu Hanmou also telegraphed: "I was shocked to learn of Mr. Yingbai's death. The country has lost a worthy man, and everyone is deeply saddened. I hope you will restrain your grief and accept the changes to comfort his spirit."

Shanghai-Hangzhou Long-Distance Telephone Line Currently Under Repair

Expected to be Completed Next Month

The Shanghai-Hangzhou long-distance telephone line originally had two pairs of wires, A and B. Due to years of neglect, they have suffered considerable damage. It is learned that the Ministry of Communications, aware of this, has begun repairs. Therefore, only the A line has been actually in operation in recent days. The Shanghai-Hangzhou telephone service is quite developed, often leading to congestion. According to telephone bureau sources, the repair work is expected to be completed next month.

National Products Groups Hold Joint Meeting Yesterday

Contributing Opinions to the Ministry of Industry, Requesting Increased Capital for Expansion of Chain Operations

In view of the small scale of the National Products Chain Company and its inability to accommodate the majority of domestic product manufacturers, the National Products Groups of this city, fearing biased treatment after its establishment, convened a joint meeting of all domestic product groups and factories in the city yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, convened by the China National Products Joint Association, to seek a solution. Several important resolutions were passed. Details are as follows:

Representatives Attending Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, the China National Products Manufacturers Joint Association held a joint meeting of National Products Groups. The attendees included Xu Xiaochu, Liu Zhongying, and Zhou Zhaolin from the China National Products Manufacturers Joint Association; Cao Zhigong and Wan Futian from the Civil National Products Year Movement; Wang Hanqiang from the China National Products Maintenance Association; Lu Xingzhuang and Ma Jisheng from the Shanghai National Products Factory Joint Association; Zhu Yangwu from the China Products Improvement Society; and representatives from over 80 factories, including Taikang Company, Greater China Rubber Factory, Jiuxin Enamel Factory, China National Products Company, Huatong Electric Appliance Factory, and Minsheng Rubber Factory, totaling over 100 people. Wang Hanqiang was elected as chairman, and Zhou Zhaolin served as recorder.

Chairman's Report After the customary greetings, the chairman reported the significance of the meeting, stating that Wu, Minister of Industry of the National Economic Construction Association, had initiated the organization of the National Products Chain Company to promote domestic products, which was commendable. However, after reviewing the organizational regulations of the company and the composition of the preparatory committee, it appeared that the company would only support a small number of factories and would not be able to fully accommodate the majority of factories. To protect the interests of the majority of small and medium-sized factories, this association, fearing biased treatment and imbalanced development of the domestic products industry after the company's establishment, proposed that all attendees express their opinions to gather wisdom and benefit, collect public opinion, and advise the government to adopt and implement them to universally promote and achieve common development.

Resolutions After the chairman's report, the following resolutions were discussed and passed: (1) Petition the Ministry of Industry to expand the scope of the National Products Chain Company and increase the stipulated capital, which seemed insufficient, to 10 million yuan, with the government subscribing to 40% of the shares and the remaining 60% to be subscribed and raised by national product groups, chambers of commerce, national product factories, the financial community, and those enthusiastic about national products in various provinces and cities. (2) Petition the Ministry of Industry to state that the appointment of preparatory committee members for the chain company should be extended to national product groups, chambers of commerce, national product factories, and those enthusiastic about national products in various provinces and cities. (3) Jointly issue a declaration by national product groups requesting expansion of the organization. (4) Notify the factories under the various associations about the opinions of the National Products Chain Company for transmission to the Ministry for adoption. (5) Elect Cao Zhigong and Zhou Zhaolin to draft the declaration and official documents. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Ge Gu's Cold Weather, Ice Surrounds the Tai Shun, Please Send an Icebreaker for Assistance, Xin Ming Can Sail South

Regarding Tianjin, the weather has been severe for days. Yesterday, various shipping companies in Shanghai received telegrams from Tianjin stating that the waters inside Dagu Port had frozen. Starting from the 6th, the ice layer in the port between Dagu and Tanggu was very thick, hindering the passage of ships. The Tai Shun, a ship of the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, with a deadweight of 1,962 tons, a length of 265 feet, and a draft of 16 feet 8 inches, had loaded a large shipment of grain and sundries from Shanghai to Tianjin. Yesterday morning, the ship sailed from Dagu Port and reached Gegu, located midway between Da Zha and Tanggu. Due to the thick ice layer in the port, the Tai Shun, lacking icebreaking equipment and having been built in 1896, now 40 years old, was unable to break through the thick, hard ice and was surrounded by ice. The entire ship was frozen and unable to proceed. Fearing danger to the crew, they telegraphed Shanghai yesterday to report the situation. At the same time, shipowner Sha Zengjia urgently telegraphed the Tianjin branch to request that an icebreaker be sent to Gegu to guide the Tai Shun to Zizhulin. The branch also telegraphed Tianjin for assistance. According to those familiar with the Beiyang waterway, if there is no strong northwest wind and if the temperature in Tianjin continues to drop, navigation will be at risk of being blocked by ice. It is reported that the Xin Ming, which had been blocked for six or seven days, was able to sail south yesterday due to a slight increase in the water level at Dagu Port.

Page 11

City Chamber of Commerce and Others Send Representatives to Petition for the Release of Detained Rice Boats, Gu Xinyi to Go to Zhenjiang This Morning to Petition the Provincial Government, Rice Detained for Days Has Reached Over 40,000 Dan

Since Qingpu, Jinshan, and other counties under the Jiangsu Provincial Government have been detaining rice boats, a total of over 200 boats have been detained as of yesterday, carrying approximately 40,000 dan of rice. This has caused the Suzhou Creek, at the border between Shanghai and Jiangsu, to be crowded with detained rice boats, obstructing navigation. The Shanghai Soybean and Rice Industry believes that the detention of rice boats by Qingpu and other counties is inconsistent with the interim measures for food regulation passed by the Executive Yuan, which stipulate that food should be allowed to circulate freely within China to balance supply and demand, and that Shanghai's food supply is also affected. Therefore, they requested assistance from the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Local Association. The two associations agreed to the request and sent Gu Xinyi and others to Zhenjiang this morning to petition the Jiangsu Provincial Government for the release of the detained rice boats destined for Shanghai and to prevent future detentions. If this fails, they will go to Nanjing to petition the Executive Yuan. According to Gu, Shanghai's 3 million residents need 12,000 dan of rice per day. Since Shanghai is not a rice-producing area, it relies on continuous supplies from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and other provinces. If Jiangsu continues to detain rice boats bound for Shanghai, Shanghai's food supply will be greatly affected. The letters from the Local Association and others are recorded below.

Letters and Telegrams from the Local Association

The Local Association requested the Governors of Jiangsu and Zhejiang to release the detained rice boats. The letter to Chairman Chen of Jiangsu stated: "Chairman Guofu, I acknowledge receipt of the attached letter from the Shanghai Soybean and Rice Industry Association, stating that Qingpu, Jinshan, Jiading, and other counties have detained rice boats leaving for Shanghai. I telegraphed your government on the [date] of last month and the [date] of this month to request that you order their release. It is now reported that approximately 200 ships carrying rice from Changshu, Wuxi, Wuxian, Wujiang, Kunshan, and other counties passing through Jiading County's Jiwang Temple area have been detained, obstructing the Songjiang waterway. The Shanghai rice market is experiencing a disruption of supply, with some businesses already suspended and others inevitably raising prices and hoarding, causing widespread panic. It is believed that the free flow of grain was decided by the Executive Yuan long ago. Shanghai has a large population and requires a large amount of rice, which is supplied by other provinces. The current situation is even more urgent. Therefore, I am sending this letter with representatives from the association, Mr. Gu Xinyi, Mr. [?], and Mr. Jiang Jingwen, to present the case in person. I respectfully request a meeting. We are grateful. We wish you peace. Shanghai Local Association, December 7, 1936." Another telegram was sent to the Zhejiang Provincial Government: "On [date], we received a telegram from the Shanghai Grain, Oil, and Cake Industry Association reporting that Yueqing and Pingyang counties had intercepted rice boats and requested that we investigate and order their release. We have received a letter from the association stating that 9,700 bags of white rice have been detained in the two counties for a long time and have gradually become moldy, and that the grain merchants are urgently demanding payment, making it difficult for them to turn over funds. They also stated that 5,000 dan of rice handled by Da Cheng in Zhenhai was also intercepted. Please expedite the release of these cases. It is believed that merchants are following the central government's decision to allow the free flow of grain and that it is not appropriate to obstruct the export of rice. Most of the rice market in Shanghai has been suspended due to a shortage of goods. If the ban is not lifted, not only will merchants face hardship, but it may also affect public order. We are sending this telegram again to request that your government order the counties detaining rice to release them separately and strictly order them not to repeat such incidents in the future. We urgently present this matter and respectfully request a response. Shanghai Local Association."

Detained Rice Boats Disrupt Traffic

Since Jiading County detained rice boats coming to Shanghai, the section of the Wusong River from Jiwang Temple to the Xinkai River has been crowded with ships, extending for over ten li. All inland river ferries traveling through the Wusong River to Wuxi, Changzhou, Changshu, Zhujiajiao, Qingpu, Shatou, and other places have been disrupted for five days. According to Wang Jianping, Director-General of the Inland River Shipping Industry Association of this city, the affected ferries are in a difficult situation to move forward or backward. All shipping companies operating on the Wusong River have been forced to suspend operations due to a lack of available ships, resulting in enormous losses from delayed passengers and cargo. The association has telegraphed the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing, the Jiangsu Provincial Government in Zhenjiang, the Mayor of Shanghai Wu, and the County Magistrate of Jiading Guo today to request that they take steps to resolve the situation. The original telegrams sent by the association to the Ministry of Communications and the Provincial Government are recorded below: "To the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing and the Jiangsu Provincial Government in Zhenjiang, since Jiading detained rice boats, traffic on the Wusong River has been disrupted for five days. Inland river ferries have all been suspended. Please order the unblocking to maintain traffic. Shanghai Inland River Shipping Industry Association."

City Party Headquarters Also Telegraphed a Request

The Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters believes that there have been frequent disasters in recent years, and the farmers' economy is exhausted. Although the provinces of Jiangnan and Central China were fortunate to have a bumper harvest this year, several provinces in the Northwest are still barren, and the supply does not meet the demand. This is enough to supply the national food supply, but there should be no exports to avoid domestic shortages during the lean months of next year. In order to maintain the people's food supply, the Party Headquarters telegraphed the Central Party Headquarters yesterday to request that the Executive Yuan be informed to instruct all customs offices to strictly prohibit the export of grain, to allow the free flow of domestic grain, and to urge the Jiangsu Provincial Government to implement the release of rice boats detained in Jiading as soon as possible to maintain the food supply of Shanghai residents.

National Products Joint Venture Company: Active Preparation Status, Stipulating 15 Standing Committee Members, Establishing an Office in Shanghai

The preparatory committee for the China National Products United Business Co., Ltd., jointly established by the National Economic Construction Movement Committee General Association, the initiators, the China National Products Production and Sales Association, and the National Products Company Introduction Office, the National United Office, was established in Beijing on the 4th. The committee members from this city returned to Shanghai one after another. According to reports, a standing committee meeting will be held within days to appoint personnel responsible for the secretariat, etc., and work can then be started. Details are recorded as follows:

Regulations for Staff

When the preparatory committee of the National Products Joint Venture Company was established, Minister of Industry Wu Dingchang, as chairman, delivered an opening speech, reporting on the purpose and process of establishing the joint venture company, and passed the outline of the preparation and the charter of the preparatory committee, which has been reported in previous newspapers. It is now known that the preparatory committee has stipulated 15 standing committee members, to be appointed by the National Economic Construction Committee, and one chairman will be designated. It is heard that the notice has been internally decided and will be sent out within days. The first meeting will be convened in Beijing within this week. At that time, a vice chairman of the standing committee will be elected. The company will establish a secretariat in Nanjing, and the position of director will be appointed by the chairman. An office will be established in Shanghai, and the directors of the office and the heads of the general affairs, design, and finance groups will be appointed by the standing committee. The meeting will also pass the shareholding regulations, etc., to facilitate public recruitment of capital. In the future, if the shares subscribed by various parties exceed one-third, the Ministry of Industry will allow the transfer from official shares, so that national merchants can universally participate.

Charter of the Preparatory Committee

The original text of the preparatory committee charter is recorded below: (1) This association is named the Preparatory Committee of China National Products United Business Co., Ltd. (2) This association prepares for the establishment of this company based on the outline of the company's preparation. (3) This association is located within the General Association of the National Economic Construction Movement Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Economic Construction Committee) in Nanjing, and an office is established in Shanghai. (4) In addition to the director, standing committee member, and general manager of the Economic Construction General Association as ex officio members, this association is organized by employing and appointing a number of the following members: (1) A number of people appointed by the General Association. (2) From the directors and board members of the China National Products Production and Sales Association and the National Products Company Introduction Office, the National United Office (hereinafter referred to as the United Office), a number of people are employed by the Economic Construction General Association. (3) From other industrial and commercial circles, a number of people are employed by the Economic Construction General Association. (4) From the banking industry, a number of people are employed by the Economic Construction General Association. (5) This association has 15 standing committee members, designated by the Economic Construction General Association from among the members. (6) This association has one chairman, filled by the director of the standing committee member or the general manager of the Economic Construction General Association. The vice chairman is elected by the standing committee members. (7) This association establishes a secretariat in Nanjing, with one secretary director appointed by the chairman from among the standing committee members, who handles the following matters under the direction of the chairman: (1) Matters related to contact with the central and local governments. (2) Matters related to contact with the office. (3) Matters related to the convening and holding of meetings of this association. (4) Matters not belonging to the office. This association establishes an office in Shanghai, with one office director and three groups: general affairs, design, and finance, each with one group leader, all elected by the standing committee members to handle the following matters separately: (1) Matters related to the recruitment and collection of commercial shares. (2) Matters related to contact with established national product companies in various places for joint operations. (3) Matters related to designing and organizing new companies in various places. (4) Matters related to investigating the national product market in various places. (5) Matters related to coordinating production, sales, and finance by the banking group. (6) Matters related to searching for national product trade talents. (7) Matters related to the preparation and formulation of various regulations and methods, and all matters that should be handled before the establishment of the company. (8) The necessary preparatory expenses of this association, after being approved for expenditure by the chairman, are advanced separately by the Economic Construction General Association and the United Office and will be returned immediately after the establishment of the company. Other office staff salaries and application postal, telegraphic, stationery, and social expenses, if in the secretariat, are borne by the Economic Construction General Association, and if in the office, are borne by the United Office. No expenditure will be made. The chairman, standing committee members, secretary, director, office director, and group leaders are all unpaid. (9) The preparation of this association is temporarily limited to December 31, 1936. All preparatory matters should be completed within the deadline. When the founding meeting of this company is held, this association will be cancelled immediately. (10) This charter will be announced and implemented after being approved by the director of the standing committee member of the Economic Construction General Association.

State-Run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Opens Joint Transport, Documentary Bills, and Goods Delivery, Implementing Direct Joint Transport Between Shantou, Guangdong, Qingdao, Tianjin, and Shanghai, and Deciding to Collect Payment for Goods on Behalf of Customers Starting January 1st

In order to seek convenience for cargo transportation and passengers, the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has not only handled direct joint transport of water and land between ports such as Shantou, Guangdong, Qingdao, Tianjin, and Shanghai, and opened regular scheduled flights to Lianyun Port, but also implemented the opening of documentary bills and the collection of payment for goods on behalf of customers, creating a new record for state-run shipping joint transport. Details are recorded as follows:

Direct Joint Transport

In the past, the joint transport of water and land cargo on the Longhai Railway, all cargo exported from the Longhai Railway was transported by China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Shantou, Guangdong, Qingdao, Tianjin, and Shanghai. However, cargo imported into the Longhai Railway, except for direct transport between Shanghai and Qingdao, required goods from other places such as Shantou, Guangdong, and Tianjin to be first reported to Shanghai for transport and then transshipped to Longhai. The handling time for transportation procedures was inevitably delayed. In order to facilitate merchants and speed up cargo transportation, the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will transport joint transport cargo from Shantou, Guangdong, and Tianjin to Longhai. It only needs to sign a transport bill without using transshipment procedures for direct export. The cargo bill will be mailed by the local branch to the consignee at the destination. If transported to Lianyungang, it can also pass through Longhai. According to the railway joint transport transferring to Pinghan and Jinpu Roads, it can be transported. The scheduled flights for joint transport are stipulated to depart from Shanghai to Lianyungang on the 2nd, 6th, 9th, 12th, 16th, 19th, 22nd, 26th, and 29th of each month, and from Lianyungang to Shanghai on the 1st, 4th, 7th, 11th, 14th, 17th, 21st, 24th, and 27th.

Collecting Payment for Goods on Behalf of Customers

In order to facilitate the settlement of payments for goods between merchants in two places, the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has specifically decided to collect payment for goods on behalf of customers starting on January 1st of next year. If a merchant in place B purchases goods from a merchant in place A and has not yet paid, the goods from place A can be transported to place B for the merchant to receive, and the merchant in place A will issue a payment bill, which will be settled and collected by personnel dispatched by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company without any handling fees, so that merchants can benefit from time and economy.

Documentary Bills and Goods Delivery

The state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has stipulated the "Notice to Merchants on Documentary Bills for Responsible Joint Transport of Water and Land Cargo," totaling 17 articles, which are summarized as follows: (1) This delivery order is a valuable security and has the same value as cash and can be used for collateralized lending or trading. Therefore, for the person delivering the goods, regardless of whether they are the consignee listed on the delivery order, as long as they hold the delivery order within the validity period of the delivery order and have the transfer column of the delivery order formally signed by the original consignor or the person signed by the original consignor, they have the right to deliver the goods. However, when the original consignor signs, they should also affix the same seal in the transfer column as the original consignment note and cargo ticket notice. (2) The validity period of the delivery order is limited to half a year from the date of issue. (6) For all goods for which delivery orders are issued, the delivery order must be submitted before the goods can be delivered. However, if the delivery orders are lost, the goods can be delivered upon expiration after formal declaration, or the goods can be delivered with a bank guarantee. Those who deliver the goods upon expiration must provide a guarantee and receive the goods within ten days after the expiration of the delivery order. Those who deliver the goods with a guarantee must pay cash for the total amount of the goods' value, freight, and miscellaneous fees listed on the delivery order, plus 30% of the total amount, and request the stationmaster of the station where the goods are located or the manager of the shipping bureau to receive the goods. Those who deliver the goods with a bank guarantee must obtain a "Bank Guarantee Letter" from a bank recognized by the railway or shipping bureau and request the stationmaster of the station where the goods are located or the manager of the shipping bureau to receive the goods. The amount of the bank guarantee should be the same as the total amount stipulated for the guaranteed delivery of goods. (9) The freight for all goods for which delivery orders are issued shall be paid in advance in principle. If the railway or shipping bureau allows payment on arrival, and no one claims the goods after they have arrived at the destination station or port, or the consignee refuses to accept the goods, the consignor shall still be responsible for paying the freight. (11) The railway or shipping bureau is responsible for compensating for losses of water and land transport goods for which delivery orders are issued as follows: (A) For losses caused by railway transportation and storage, the railway shall be responsible for compensation in accordance with the railway regulations. (B) For losses caused by ship transportation and storage, the shipping bureau shall be responsible for compensation in accordance with the shipping regulations. If the customs has special regulations and methods, they shall be followed. The transfer of ten liability items shall be based on the signing of the certificate of acceptance. (C) When the responsibility for the loss is unclear, the railway and the shipping bureau shall jointly be responsible for compensation, and the proportion shall be recognized according to the freight earned by the batch of goods. However, the maximum amount of compensation for which the railway is liable shall be the amount that should be shared and compensated according to the proportion of freight, and the maximum amount of compensation for which the shipping bureau is liable shall be 350 silver dollars per piece. (12) All claims for compensation for losses of goods must be submitted within six months from the date the goods arrive at the destination station or port. Overdue claims will not be accepted. (15) When goods are auctioned due to price changes, after deducting freight and miscellaneous fees, if there is any remaining payment, the merchant may provide a guarantee and receive the goods at any time within one year after the auction is established. If there is a shortfall, they must also be responsible for making up the difference. (16) The railway and shipping bureau shall be responsible for all compensation for goods for which delivery orders are issued, except for the following losses: (A) Those belonging to natural disasters and events that cannot be resisted by human power. (B) Those caused by improper packaging. (C) Those caused by natural burning, reduction, or corruption of goods. (D) Those caused by epidemic prevention, taxation, war, mass riots, and legal sanctions. (E) Those belonging to water and fire disasters. (F) Those belonging to the fault of the merchant or cannot prove that it is definitely the fault of the railway and shipping bureau.

Swire Tugboat and Hai Zhen Steamer Collide, Both Sides Suffer Major Losses, Responsibility for the Accident Must Be Decided Impartially

Swire Company's large tugboat, Chuling, was towing three large iron barges loaded with tung oil from Hankou to Shanghai. At 7:14 pm on the 5th of this month, it arrived at the Faot Buoy river cylinder outside the Wusongkou battery. At the same time, the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Hai Zhen steamer (weighing 3,406 tons, 71, ship length 34 feet 3 inches, draft 17 feet 6 inches) was sailing to Shantou and Hong Kong. It was just sailing to the Faot Buoy river cylinder outside the Wusong battery when the Zhu Ting tugboat was also sailing with three barges. The Zhu Ting tugboat was tying the 13th barge to the tugboat to travel together, and the other two barges were being towed behind. When the three barges arrived in front of the river cylinder, their hulls turned and came around the river cylinder. The Zhu Ting number towed the two barges behind, and the wire cable was extended to more than 500 feet. The Hai Zhen steamer was near the river cylinder. It was observed that the waterway there and the river cylinder occupied about 750 feet, and the Zhu Ting's tow cable was across the waterway for 500 feet, completely blocking the route. Under this situation, the sailors urgently sounded the whistle and ordered the Zhu Ting and each barge to stop quickly. However, each barge had lost its position to advance or retreat and could not avoid it, but the Zhu Ting still drove across and violently collided with the Hai Zhen. The 13th iron barge, which was tied to the Zhu Ting towing transmission, had the most violent impact with the bow of the Hai Zhen steamer, causing the left side of the 13th iron barge to break immediately. Seawater flooded into the barge, and the loss of tung oil and cargo was huge. The barge was hit, and because the vibration force was very large, the Zhu Ting tugboat retreated backward. The two barges behind were advancing on the tow cable at a distance of 500 feet, so they were struck by the Zhu Ting and the 13th barge and collided with each other, causing the two barges behind to also suffer serious injuries. As for the bow of the Hai Zhen steamer, because it collided with an iron barge, four iron plates in the head cabin on the right side were dented very deeply, and the water cabin inside the bow (behind the anchor chain) was also broken, so the damage was also extremely serious. After the accident, both sides stopped the transmission. On one hand, the shipowner of the Hai Zhen steamer, Hu Xiyuan, and the towing personnel of the Zhu Ting jointly inspected the damaged areas. It took a total of six hours. After the situation was proved, the Zhu Ting towed the three barges to Shanghai to report to the company. All three barges were damaged, and the loss of cargo was huge. Yesterday, Swire reported to the cargo owners and carefully checked the amount of damage. The total amount is currently unknown. The Hai Zhen steamer's shipowner, Hu Xiyuan, telegraphed the truth of the accident to Shanghai in the morning of the 6th. Because the ship could still sail, it sailed to Shantou as usual. As for the water leaks and damage to the hull, it will be inspected after the goods are unloaded in Shantou. It is also unknown whether the goods have been damaged or destroyed. Yesterday, the bureau received a telegram from the sailors stating that the responsibility for this incident lies entirely with the Zhu Ting tugboat for violating the navigation regulations. Towing a ship with a 500-foot cable and blocking the route means that the responsibility for the accident lies entirely with the tugboat. Therefore, the bureau sent a letter to Swire requesting to reserve all compensation responsibilities. As for Swire, there has been no response. If the Navigation Administration Bureau makes a fair judgment, because the Zhu Ting belongs to a British merchant, it is feared that Swire may not agree. In the future, Chinese and foreign experts may be hired to form a fair judgment committee to handle the case.

Sentenced to Life Imprisonment

Hua Shih Hao, a martial arts instructor from Hubei, residing at No. 51, Jiahe Lane, Hart Road, had a gambling-related feud with Yang Hanzhang, a fellow townsman from Qingbei Tongxiang Association's club at No. 46 in the same lane. Fire Consumes Three Homes in Gujia Lane, Niuzhuang Road

Caused by Birthday Candles

Inside a shikumen building at No. 3, Jifu Lane, Gujia Lane, Niuzhuang Road, in the Public Concession, lived three cotton fabric firms: Zheng Changxiang (upstairs), Heng Changxiang (downstairs eastern wing), and Qi Changxiang (western wing). The owners all lived in the shops with their families. The other day, Heng Changxiang's owner celebrated his 60th birthday with a banquet. Late into the night, after the guests had left, they forgot to extinguish the birthday candles. Around 2:00 AM yesterday, the remaining candle fell onto the table, immediately igniting the wooden walls. In an instant, flames raged. Fortunately, Zheng Changxiang's wife was getting up to use the toilet and noticed the fire. She shouted an alarm, and the men, women, old, and young of the three families, along with the employees, were awakened from their sleep and fled in panic. Most did not have time to put on clothes. Fortunately, a tragic disaster was averted, but the goods in the stores, as well as valuables and luggage, could not be retrieved, and they escaped with their lives. The losses were enormous. Neighboring shops were spared due to the swift arrival and firefighting efforts of the fire brigade.

Public Rickshaw Pullers Must Wear Numbered Jackets and Raincoats

To improve the lives of rickshaw pullers, Article 16 of the Public Concession's rickshaw licensing regulations stipulates that each rickshaw owner must provide two numbered jackets and one raincoat. This matter was announced to all rickshaw companies by the Rickshaw Committee in early September of this year, and standard numbered jackets and raincoats were made and displayed at the rickshaw licensing office for rickshaw companies to follow. However, to ease the financial burden on the companies, existing usable numbered jackets and raincoats, even if they did not fully meet the prescribed standards, could be submitted to the licensing office for inspection and stamping for use. A total of 14,274 numbered jackets and 3,243 raincoats were approved under this arrangement. The remaining number required was fully supplied by mid-November. From now on, all public rickshaw pullers must wear numbered jackets to pull their rickshaws, and the number on the back of the jacket and raincoat must match the number of the rickshaw. Furthermore, the number of new-style public rickshaws in the Public Concession has reached 3,700, and it is expected to reach 4,000 by the end of this year.

Li Guojie Case: Execution Hearing Continued Yesterday; Li and Duan Ling Headed to Beiping; Court Approves Postponement for Further Interrogation

Li Guojie, former General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, was sentenced to eight months of imprisonment with probation after the court's three trials concluded, for mortgaging the four wharves to the China General Edison Company and forfeiting navigation rights to foreigners. At that time, Li had allegedly bribed Supervisor Chen Fumu with 700,000 taels from the mortgage loan. To date, the principal and interest have reached over 1.2 million yuan. During the execution hearing in June, Yu Qiaqing and Li Sihao posted bail for Li to handle the matter, but no money has been paid to date. The creditor, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, also investigated and found only a small portion of the assets, less than one-tenth of the amount owed. Therefore, they continued to pursue the case and requested the court to declare Li Guojie bankrupt. However, Li, claiming to be a person of status, expressed his unwillingness. The court ordered him to provide assets within half a month, but Li still did not comply. Yesterday, Yu Lude, the judge of the court execution division, again convened a hearing. The defendant, Li Guojie, did not appear. Lawyer Jiang Yiping, representing Li, stated that the debtor had been assigned as a member and chief receptionist of Duan's funeral committee and had departed for Beiping today to transport the coffin, hence his absence. He requested a one-month extension. The judge asked if the defendant had contacted China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Jiang replied, "No." The judge asked if he had presented his assets. Jiang replied, "There are no fixed assets." The judge asked why he was delaying the matter despite the prior summons. He added that the funeral arrangements could be handled perfectly well even without Li Guojie. Jiang replied that Duan's funeral committee was organized by Chairman Jiang, who appointed Li as a member, and that the municipal government had sent an official letter to the court stating this. The judge said that the municipal government could not advise on this case, and that the court had received the letter but had replied stating that Li Guojie's reasons for requesting a postponement were not justified. Lawyer Jiang immediately stated that Li was indeed dispatched and not trying to delay the matter, requesting approval for a change of date. The judge then approved a postponement to a date determined by telegram to Li in Beiping, giving him the time required for travel to return. Just as the judge was about to adjourn, Jiang Heyi, the lawyer representing the plaintiff, arrived, stating that he was slightly delayed due to another court appearance at the First Special Court. The judge then showed Jiang the municipal government's letter and reply and instructed, "If he does not appear, we will have to handle it according to the law." He then asked if China Merchants Steam Navigation Company had investigated Li's assets. Jiang replied, "We are still investigating. As soon as we have verified it, we will report." The court then adjourned.

Robbery at Sanpailou Yesterday

At 5:15 PM yesterday, four robbers suddenly arrived at Yongxingxiang Embroidery Children's Hat Shop, opened by Qiu Decheng, a local resident, at No. 96, Shengjia Lane, Sanpailou, inside the city. They were armed with a pistol, the authenticity of which was uncertain. One robber wore a black jacket and trousers, one wore a gray gown and was of large build, and the other two wore blue jackets and trousers. They forbade anyone from making a sound and asked the shop owner for money for dinner. Unable to find the hidden silver, they became anxious and robbed a gold ring and three sewing machines, worth over 100 yuan in total, before fleeing. Afterward, the shop owner reported the incident to the police station in charge, requesting an investigation.

Recent News from the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association

New Board of Directors Convenes Meeting

The third board of directors of the Shanghai Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association was reorganized upon the decision of the Public Works Department board meeting, with three representatives each from the Public Works Department, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, and the Chinese Ratepayers' Association. The following nine individuals have been nominated by the three organizations: Chen Tingrui, Yan Chengde, Cheng Xiechun, Jin Runyang, Zhou Bangjun, Ge Jechen, Lu Weili, Shen Tilan, and Tong Xingmen, and they have been appointed by the Public Works Department. They convened their first meeting of this term at 4:30 PM the other day (the third day) in the Public Works Department conference hall. Except for Shen Tilan, who was absent due to an educational inspection in southern China, all others were present. Dr. Chen Tingrui was elected chairman. Former chairman Mr. Massey will continue to serve as chairman of the association's management committee. All directors, recognizing the importance of their mission, are committed to serving and sacrificing for the welfare of the 40,000 members and their families. They are willing to fully support the current Director-General Zhang Dengying and all staff to facilitate the association's work. A letter of appreciation will be sent to each of the retiring committee members from the previous term in recognition of their achievements. The recent statistical reports of the work in the past few months and the account statements from August to October show that the association's work has made special progress, which all directors find satisfactory. According to recent statistics, the association's clinic has served 55,000 rickshaw pullers and their family members. The number of workers involved in October was 324,640. Important matters discussed at the meeting are listed below: (1) The resignations of the deputy director-general and two other directors were approved. (2) The issue of fees for rickshaw pullers to register and obtain permits. (3) A plan to build two additional buildings in addition to the purchased cemetery land for deceased members. (4) The issue of the medical director's position. (5) Written publicity. Furthermore, the association's constitution will be revised due to the reorganization of the board of directors. Jin Runyang, Tong Xingmen, Zhou Bangjun, and Chen Tingrui were appointed as special committee members to conduct preliminary research and submit it to a joint meeting of the board of directors and the management committee for approval.

Student Steals Perfume Bottle in Sincere Company: Fined 50 Yuan After Interrogation

At 2:05 PM the other day, a young man suddenly stole a bottle of perfume and a perfume atomizer, worth 10 yuan, from the cosmetics department of Sincere Company at No. 680, Nanjing Road. He was spotted by the company's employees, who immediately arrested him and took him to the Laozha Police Station. Under questioning by Chinese detectives Feng Xiushan and Bao Shanji, he revealed his name as Qu Keming, 17, a Shanghai native and a student at a certain school. His father, Qu Xiechang, works at the Jardine Egg Factory and lives at No. 51, Lane 478, Xinzha Road. His family is well-off. He fully admitted to stealing the perfume. He was detained. This morning, he was sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu explained the case and prosecuted him for theft under Article 320 of the Criminal Law. Then, Chen Wenbing, an employee of Sincere Company, testified about Qu's theft. Qu Xiechang also turned himself in, stating that his son had always been well-behaved and that this incident might have been due to nerves, requesting the court to be lenient. Under interrogation, Qu Keming confessed to the theft. Judge Pan Zhenti verified the confession and sentenced Qu to a fine of 50 yuan and ordered the return of the stolen goods to the owner.

Zhang Yinkui Transports a Sack of Cigarette Ash Weighing Over 100 Pounds by Rickshaw: Arrested and Sent to Court

Zhang Yinkui, from Tongzhou, at 8:20 AM the other day, placed a sack of opium ash, weighing 125 pounds, on the rickshaw he was pulling. While traveling near the intersection of Tiantong Road and North Sichuan Road, he was spotted by Chinese detective Tang Qingfu and No. 2283, who found his behavior suspicious and stopped him. Under questioning, it was revealed that the ash was taken from a trash bin in Sanguantang Lane, Huaxun Road, by the order of Li Bingchen, the owner of the Jizhitang Pharmacy at No. 236, North Shanxi Road, for whom Zhang was a rickshaw puller. Detective Tang took Zhang Yinkui and the sack of ash to the Hongkou Police Station and investigated the Jizhitang Pharmacy. It was claimed that the owner, Mr. Li, was out and had not returned. Yesterday morning, the criminal Zhang was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Public Works Department lawyer Zhang Shizhu explained the case, requesting a postponement for further investigation. Then, detective Tang Chang reported the details of the arrest and presented the evidence. The defendant's confession was evasive. Judge Xiao Xiefei ordered him to remain in custody for further investigation.

New Pharmaceutical Industry: Notice Regarding Counterfeit Drugs

The National Federation of New Pharmaceutical Industry Associations yesterday issued a notice to all members nationwide, stating: "Esteemed colleagues, the authenticity of drugs is crucial to patients' lives. However, unscrupulous individuals often counterfeit popular over-the-counter medicines and sell them in various ports, damaging the interests of the manufacturers. This is a small matter compared to the harm caused to the public, which is immense. The sale of counterfeit drugs damages customer trust and undermines the reputation of manufacturers and the business of sellers. If this is not thoroughly clarified, it will be detrimental to manufacturers, sellers, and buyers alike. Recently, it was reported that the Shanghai Special District cracked a case involving Gui Yaohua and Huang Futang of the Dadong Pharmacy manufacturing counterfeit products. Fifteen boxes of various counterfeit drugs were seized, and the extent of their harm is imaginable. Although the Dadong case has been solved, there is no guarantee that others will not continue to manufacture counterfeit drugs and test the law. Counterfeiting drugs violates Article 205 of Chapter 11 of the Criminal Law, which deals with crimes endangering public safety: 'Those who manufacture, sell, or display for sale items harmful to hygiene shall be sentenced to imprisonment or detention and may also be fined up to 1,000 yuan.' Moreover, due to the counterfeiting, Article 268 of Chapter 18, which deals with crimes harming agriculture, industry, and commerce, is also violated: 'Those who counterfeit registered or unregistered trademarks or trade names with the intention of deceiving others shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to two years and may also be fined up to 1,000 yuan.' Those who sell the counterfeit drugs, whether due to carelessness or greed for profit, also violate Article 269 of the Criminal Law. Therefore, the second general meeting of the association's members resolved to protect the reputation and rights of the industry and to safeguard the lives and health of the people. All members should pay close attention. If anyone discovers the manufacture of counterfeit drugs, they should sever ties with them to avoid being implicated. This notice is hereby issued for your information."

Continuously Gloomy and Cold Weather in the City

Since last Saturday, the city has not seen sunlight all day. After a light snowfall in between, although there was a brief appearance of sunlight at noon the next day, it was immediately obscured. Therefore, the weather has been unusually gloomy and cold. Yesterday was even worse. From morning to evening, the sky was covered with dense clouds. Around 1:15 PM, there was another light snowfall, followed by rain that continued into the evening. According to general forecasts, it is feared that the Great Cold is approaching.

Cloth Fraud Case: Criminal Chen Hongxiang Arrested

Chen Hongxiang, a native of Ningbo, 28 years old this year, falsely established the Dafeng Cloth Company at No. 24, Baoxing Lane, Fada Road, last year. He successively defrauded eight cloth factories or brokers, including Xi Yuntai and Tang Wanqi, of cloth, linen, and poplin worth 1,530 yuan and more. He sold the goods, spent the money, abandoned the company, and fled without a trace. The victims reported the matter to the French Concession Police, requesting an investigation, but he could not be found. Recently, Chen was hiding at No. 25, Peifu Lane, Lagena Road, in the French Concession. Chen owed Lyu Rongqing (28 years old), a broker from Jiaxing, 7 yuan in commission for advertising business that he ran in addition to the Dafeng Cloth Company. Recently, Lyu met Chen, and Chen invited Lyu to his home, intending to start another business. The afternoon before yesterday, Lyu asked Chen for the old debt of 7 yuan in commission. The two had an argument, which escalated into a fight. Lyu was beaten by Chen. Lyu reported the matter to the French Concession Police. Detective Wu Wengang learned that Chen was wanted under arrest warrant No. 418 issued by the Second Special Court for the cloth fraud case. He arrested Chen. Yesterday morning, Chen was sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special Court. Police lawyer Gu Shouxi explained the case and requested a postponement for further investigation before prosecuting. Judge Mi Chuzhe questioned the defendant and the witness Lyu Rongqing and ordered a postponement of 14 days for further investigation. The defendant was remanded in custody, and the witness Lyu Rongqing was ordered to appear in court for cross-examination at the next hearing.

Another Water Gambling Den Broken Up: Over a Hundred Gamblers Flee at the Sound of the Alarm; Two Injured Jumping Ashore

Balunshi, the criminal division chief of the Customs Water Police, learned the other evening that someone had secretly set up a water gambling den on the second deck of the stern of the Xianghe steamboat of the Jardine Company at Huashun Wharf in Hongkou. The gambling equipment included pai gow, big and small, and dice games. The scale was quite large. He immediately led a large number of Chinese and foreign detectives in two groups, one traveling by car along the shore to the wharf, and the other traveling by small boat to the outside of the ship. At the same time, they rushed onto the ship to make arrests. However, many lookouts were stationed around the ship. Upon seeing the detectives approach, they immediately raised the alarm. At that time, over a hundred gamblers were gathered at the gambling den, enjoying themselves. Upon hearing the alarm, they scattered and fled. Some even escaped by jumping down to the wharf from the bottom deck. Twenty-two male and female gamblers, including Ye Wo, were arrested on the spot. Among them, Jin Yusheng and Ding Xiangfa were injured while jumping onto the wharf from the side of the ship to escape. Jin broke his leg, and Ding injured his waist. They were taken to Renji Hospital by ambulance. After treatment, as their injuries were not serious, they were taken back to the police station. Yesterday morning, the police questioned the arrested criminals and ordered them to be sent to the local court for interrogation this afternoon, along with the gambling equipment and gambling money.

Train Derailment on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway: Passenger Train at 5:07 AM Arrived in Shanghai at 3:00 AM This Morning After Departing from Beijing Yesterday Afternoon

The Beijing-Shanghai Railway had a freight train derailing the other night after departing from Beijing. The train mistakenly went onto a siding near the Zhoujingxiang train station, causing two freight cars to derail. The station reported the incident to the Nanjing station, which sent a crane to lift the cars. However, it took a long time, causing the express train departing from Beijing yesterday at noon, which should have arrived in Shanghai at 8:40 PM, to be delayed until 3:40 AM this morning, a delay of seven hours.

Chinese Invention: Energy-Saving Flat Light Bulb

Long-Lasting Filament; Saves 30% Electricity

Electrician Pan Zuyin is an avid researcher with a strong background in light bulbs. He recently invented an economical flat light bulb. Due to its flat and round shape, the vacuum space is enlarged, which can extend the life of the filament, making it less likely to break. The glass shell never turns black, based entirely on scientific methods and electrical principles. It is very economical and durable. At the same time, it saves electricity and emits bright light, saving 30% more electricity than ordinary light bulbs. The copper head is plated with dazzling chrome, making it more luxurious and beautiful. The price is also very low, selling for only 10 cents of national currency each. Therefore, it is suitable for families, shops, organizations, and institutions. It is truly a rising new authority in the light bulb industry. It is exclusively managed by the China Light Bulb Company at No. 77, Hengmao Lane, Baxianqiao, French Concession, Shanghai. If customers purchase half a dozen, they can call and someone will deliver it. Local and out-of-town distributors are welcome to contact them.

Trapped by Livelihood Difficulties: Wang Shourong Commits Suicide

Wang Shourong, 49, from Suzhou, has been unemployed recently. On the 4th at 7:00 PM, he checked into room number six at the Xinglong Inn at No. 343, Baliaoqiao Street, French Concession. Trapped by livelihood difficulties, he took his own life by poisoning on the night of the 6th. At 9:00 AM on the 7th, the innkeeper Qian A'gen discovered him and reported it to the French Concession Police. He was sent to Renji Hospital, but due to severe poisoning, treatment was ineffective. He died at 1:05 PM. The hospital notified the police, who sent the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall for examination, pending a court inspection.

Public Security Bureau Cracks Down on an Agency Investigating Smuggling: Falsely Establishes a Smuggling Intelligence Office of the Ministry of Finance; Eleven Principals and Accomplices Arrested

In order to prevent smuggling, the Ministry of Finance planned to organize a smuggling investigation intelligence office in the summer of this year. Since this was never implemented, a notice was published in the newspaper on September 27 announcing the cancellation and cessation of the organization. However, Mu Shiying from Dalian, Xiong Xiangtao from Hubei, Cao Fengwu from Anhui, and others, used the name of the Ministry of Finance Smuggling Investigation Intelligence Office, which had long been discontinued and abolished, to swindle money in various districts of the city.

Pretending to be

Mu Shiying, the principal offender, falsely claimed to be the leader of the special agent team three and forged letters of appointment, taking bribes to sell official positions. The price to buy the position of a special agent team leader was 1,000 yuan in foreign currency, while a detective cost 200 yuan. Over a hundred people, intoxicated with the desire for official positions, were deceived. Liu Huai, the captain of the investigation team of the Public Security Bureau, learned of this and used prudent and strict methods to conduct a thorough investigation. Detectives pretended to be willing to pay

large sums of money

to buy official positions. After several negotiations with the principal offender Mu Shiying, it was agreed that a fee of 150 yuan would be paid to become the accountant of the fake agency. After the agreement was made, at 7:00 PM on December 5, Mu summoned the key members of the fake agency for a banquet at the Taolechun Restaurant on the second floor of No. 2, Aiduya Road, to introduce them and exchange gifts. The Public Security Bureau immediately led

a large number of detectives,

together with Chinese and foreign detectives from the Public Concession's Laozha Police Station, to Taolechun at 7:00 PM on the 5th to make arrests. They arrested the principal offender Mu Shiying, the fake leader of the third special agent team, Xiong Jiangqing (also known as Xiong Xiangtao), the fake director of general affairs of the intelligence office, and the key criminals Gan Yulin (Gan Yulin), Yan Zishan, Li Qing, Hu Zhefu, Gao Shichang, Cao Mingqi (Cao Fengwu), Shu Guanlin, and nine others.

At Mu's residence,

they found 150 yuan in foreign currency, which was the bribe money pre-marked by the fake official-seekers from the Public Security Bureau's investigation team, as well as other related important documents and fake letters of appointment. The nine criminals were taken to the Laozha Police Station and questioned about their age, origin, and address. Mu Shiying, 50 years old, from Tianjin, living at No. 1, Sijing Lane, Daling Road, Xiong Jiangqing, 61 years old, from Hubei,

living in Belle Road,

No. 677, Baoxing Lane, Gan Yulin, 41 years old, from Hunan, living at No. 222, Xinxin Lane, Pushi Road, Yan Zishan, 47 years old, from Hunan, living at the Fresh Pig Industry Association, Xuejiabang, Li Qing, 29 years old, from Nantong, living at the Fresh Pig Industry Association, Xuejiabang, Hu Zhefu, 48 years old, from Anhui, living at No. 677, Shixing Lane, Belle Road, Wo Weichang,

46 years old,

from Xuzhou, with no fixed address, Cao Mingqi, 57 years old, from Anhui, living at No. 168, Kangti Road, Shu Guanlin, 48 years old, from Danyang, living at No. 5, Yongxiang Lane, Gonghe Road. At 10:00 PM, the nine criminals and the evidence were transferred to the Public Security Bureau. At 11:00 PM, at the fake third special agent team office at No. 5, Chunhua Lane, Qiujiang Road, Zhabei, they arrested

fake detectives

Xu Shaoqing and Xu Cixiang, and seized a fake handwritten order. A piece of iron plate with the name of the fake intelligence office communication office was removed from the door. The two criminals were taken to the Public Security Bureau for custody. Xu Shaoqing, 51 years old, from Anhui, and Xu Jiaxiang, 35 years old, from Anhui, lived with Xu Shaoqing at No. 5, Chunrong Lane, Qiujiang Road. Subsequently, a large package of documents and miscellaneous items was found in Mu's residence at No. 1, Sijing Lane, Daling Road. All the criminals are currently detained in the Public Security Bureau detention center pending further investigation. The evidence is stored in the investigation team for future reference, in order to continue searching for the remaining criminals.

New and Old Shareholders Re-elect Directors and Supervisors, Amend Articles of Association, and Fully Collect Share Capital

The Shanghai Women's Commercial Savings Bank on Nanjing Road held a temporary meeting of new and old shareholders at 2 p.m. on the 6th on the second floor of the bank to discuss the increase in capital. Establishment of Buddhist Hospital

Mr. Chen Qichang of Yun Jian is well-versed in medicine. He was engaged in revolution in his early years, and later deeply felt Mr. Sun Yat-sen's saying that revolution must first revolutionize the heart. Therefore, he devoted himself to Buddhism. Last winter, he founded the Guanyin Relief Association and published the Dasheng Bao, which was praised by all parties. Recently, he has also received the support of famous monks and laymen such as Dharma Master Yinguang, Yuanying, etc., and great laymen such as Li Guandan, Jiang Yiyuan, Nie Yuntai, and Qu Wenliu, etc., to establish a Buddhist hospital, with the aim of providing food and clothing, treating laymen preferentially, relieving the poor and sick, and benefiting the public. The hospital site has been purchased at the old site of Leshan Hall at the intersection of Xiahfei Road and Jin Shenfu Road, and is currently being renovated. It is rumored that the opening will be held on the 16th of this month, and a Buddhist hall will be established on the 9th in advance, and Dharma Master Xingci will be respectfully invited to preach the Universal Gate Sutra for seven days. At that time, there will definitely be a grand occasion.

Shao Wenmei's Warmth and Devotion to Child Welfare

Saving the Money from His Grandson's One-Month Celebration to Buy Clothes for Children in the Education Center

Mr. Shao Wenmei of the yarn industry in this city recently celebrated the one-month anniversary of his grandson, and friends and relatives sent gifts. Shao planned to reciprocate with a banquet, but then decided that the Child Welfare Education Center run by the Chinese Child Welfare Association was well-managed, so he donated 400 yuan of the banquet money to the children of the center to make clothes and shoes, for the benefit of relatives and friends, and to benefit poor children. This is truly rare.

Ma Xiangbo Donates Books

To Enrich the Xiangbo Library in Danyang

Mr. Ma Xiangbo, an old man of ninety-seven, is respected by the world for his learning and morality, and he is willing to spare no effort in promoting cultural undertakings. Because the cultural undertakings in his hometown were backward, he planned to donate all his collections to the Education Bureau of Danyang and the library founded by the Danyang Association of Fellow Townsmen in Shanghai. The people in charge of the library admired Mr. Ma Xiangbo's kindness in benefiting future generations, so they named the library after Mr. Ma Xiangbo to commemorate him. They immediately appointed local officials, gentry, celebrities, and leaders of fellow townsmen abroad to organize a board of directors to prepare for the establishment. In recent months, they have received the support of party and state leaders, elders, and celebrities, and it is about to be completed. Recently, Mr. Ma Xiangbo invited Zhang Huisun, Dong Kenqian, Liu Zhemin, Han Jingqi, and Ma Yuzhang, executive directors of the Xiangbo Library in Shanghai, to a banquet at Leshan Hall in Tushanwan, and also invited fellow townsmen in Shanghai, including Chen Yuming, Liu Jingwen, Zhu Xinru, Pei Yuanding, and He Yunsheng, as well as relatives, to accompany him. During the banquet, Mr. Ma Xiangbo inquired about the library affairs in detail, and laughed loudly, looking very happy. He also comforted the people in charge of the library, and at the same time donated all his collections of books. The book list was handed over to the executive director of the library. All the books have been packed and are waiting to be transported. The donated books include various books on classics, history, philosophy, science, etc. Among them, there are many rare books, totaling tens of thousands of volumes, as well as various Shenbao newspapers, Xinwenbao newspapers, and Yishibao newspapers from previous years, as well as a bust statue of Mr. Ma Xiangbo sculpted by sculptor Jiang Xiaochian.

"Times Cartoon" Suiyuan Special Issue Published

The 32nd issue of "Times Cartoon", edited and published by Lu Shaofei, general sales agent of Shanghai Times Bookstore Company, No. 240 Xiahfei Road, was published yesterday. Regarding the current Suiyuan issue, this magazine uses cartoons to expose the inside story of this issue, without being afraid of seeking the truth, and without hesitating to make it true. Therefore, the authors, such as the photos of the bandit puppet army after Sun in Baotou, and the invasion of Sui border by Bao Zongjin in Tianjin, occupy most of the book. Those who are concerned about Suiyuan have already published as much material as possible in this magazine, which is worth reading. Social life cartoons are also attached to this issue, totaling 48 pages. Each copy costs 2 jiao, and all bookstores and newsstands sell it on consignment.

Hu Zaobin Goes to Beijing for Painting Exhibition

The painter Hu Zaobin is a hardworking young man in the modern art world. Recently, he selected his best works and held a solo exhibition of traditional Chinese paintings at the Overseas Chinese Guest House in the capital. Yesterday, Mr. Hu took his works to Beijing. The exhibition will be held from the 12th to the 15th of this month, and a large book "Collection of Hu Zaobin's Painting Exhibition" will be printed. The book emphasizes both pictures and text, and the printing is exquisite. It is a ten-page booklet. Chairman Lin Sen wrote the antithetical couplet, President Cai Yuanpei wrote the title page, Liang Dingming painted his portrait, and the text includes works by Gao Jianfu, Chen Shuren, Liu Yazi, Jiang Kanghu, Liang Dingming, Zai Yachen, Sun Fuxi, Wang Zhiyuan, and Zhang Shuqi. The paintings include 32 paintings of figures, flowers, birds, insects, beasts, as well as Western paintings, sculptures, and epigraphy by Mr. Hu.
