Overview of Industrial and Commercial Changes in Shanghai in September of the 25th Year (Continued)

— Edited by China Credit

(Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Overview, No. 39)

Here is a detailed table of the various industrial and commercial changes in Shanghai in September, for your reference:

Statistical Table of Industrial and Commercial Changes in Shanghai in September of the 25th Year (Unit: Household)

Spring and Autumn

Crabs of Jiading

— (Qingqu)

The types of crabs vary from place to place. Although the production of crabs in my hometown of Jiading is not large, they are displayed in the market from spring to summer to late autumn, almost every day, but only in varying quantities. However, there are early and late crab seasons. The northeast of the city is earlier, and the crabs are on the market before the beginning of the north wind, usually around the Mid-Autumn Festival, and the fishermen are all competing to catch them first. However, the crabs at this time have just molted, their bodies are large, but the meat is not full, and the roe is not abundant. Those who really have a fondness for holding the claws do not cherish them, thinking that they are not worthy of the famous name of the "crab with a round belly in September and a pointed belly in October." The water source of the West Gate comes from Zhangpu, the river is wide and clear, so the crabs enter the market later, but they are definitely firm and old. Generally, this time is when the oranges are yellow and the chrysanthemums are blooming, and it is the time to climb high and stretch out, and the saying "when the west wind blows, the crab legs become hard" is not false. The best crabs are those produced in the Chuobang Township in the south of the city. Although they are later, they are all fat. What is even more strange is that the Gongsunjing in the south of the township has a "工" character on its back, and the Yangjing in the east of the township has a "王" character on its back, which are faintly discernible, and their bodies are slightly larger, and their feet are slightly smaller, and their taste is more exquisite. When cooking in a pot, try putting crabs from other places in it and make a note in advance. When you open the lid, the crabs with the "工" and "王" characters must be on top, otherwise they will be on the bottom, without exception. It can be seen that the solid ones can struggle, and the hollow ones will die when heated. The difference is self-evident. According to its origin, the water of the Chuobang River is between fresh and salt, so the weight of each male crab is less than a pound, but the shell is thin and the meat is thick, and there is no fishy smell, which is truly unique. It is a pity that they are not often seen in the market, and even if they are, they are sold as counterfeits. Connoisseurs are not deceived by this. Those who want to buy them go to the countryside and make reservations with the fishermen. Although the price is slightly higher, they are not stingy. Therefore, in the current Gongsunjing and Yangjing, among the Xiao Xiao reeds on both sides of the river, the fishing lights are flickering, and the small thatched huts are like deep trenches and high fortresses, waiting for the gutless gentleman to fall into them and be bound, and then presented as captives to the general gourmets.

Orange Talk

— Wolfo

Yanzi of Qi said, "Oranges, when grown north of the Huai River, turn into trifoliate oranges." Qu Yuan's Ode to the Orange said: "The late emperor esteemed good trees, and planted orange trees as a tribute. The mandate was not far off, for they were born in the south." It can be seen that oranges have been cherished by people since ancient times. During the time of Emperor Wu of the Han Dynasty, an "orange official" was specially set up in Jiaozhi, with a rank of 200 shi, who was responsible for offering imperial oranges. This is also a glorious history of oranges. Since then, oranges have become the subject of poems, such as: "After writing, I want to inscribe three hundred oranges, and I have to wait for the frost to fill the forest in Dongting," "There are oranges in Jiangnan, and they are still in the forest in winter," "Slaves in the mountains have thousands of orange trees," etc., and I can't remember them all.

Oranges are evergreen shrubs, botanically classified as Rutaceae. They bloom with five white petals in summer and bear fruit in early winter, which is oblate in shape and green in color. After the frost falls, they turn red or yellow before they can be eaten. Since the opening of the sea ban, we have increased our enjoyment of oranges. Taking Shanghai as an example: in addition to the "Fuzhou oranges" produced in Fuzhou, there are also "Guangzhou oranges" transported from Guangzhou and "honey oranges" transported from Siam. Since honey oranges have invaded the domestic market, Fuzhou oranges, Guangzhou oranges, etc. have all been eclipsed. More than ten years ago, the calligrapher Taitaishan Nong planted thousands of orange trees on Taitaishan, known as "Taitai Honey Oranges." Because of the delicious taste of the oranges and the evaluation of the literati, the sales were very good. Unfortunately, Shan Nong was planning to promote them when he passed away, and the orange fields were abandoned. Fortunately, the people of Taizhou have learned about the benefits of planting oranges and have planted them one after another, so Taizhou honey oranges still occupy a place in the Shanghai fruit market and compete with Siamese honey oranges. Then, when we eat Taizhou honey oranges, we can't forget the pioneering work of Shan Nong. In addition to the above-mentioned areas, the orange-producing areas in our country also include "Nanfeng oranges" produced in Nanfeng County, Jiangxi, and "Dongting Reds" produced on the east and west mountains of Dongting Lake, which are also excellent oranges. It is said that the best Nanfeng oranges are those produced in Guobeiyuan, and their size is equal to Dongting Reds. Now the farmers in Guobeiyuan, Nanfeng, have organized a transportation and sales cooperative to improve the way of transporting and selling to other places, and people in Shanghai can also buy them.

The so-called "Flag Honey Oranges" produced in the United States are available in all seasons because they use scientific storage and cultivation methods. This is enough to break the saying that oranges turn into trifoliate oranges when grown north of the Huai River. Science is omnipotent, is there still any doubt?

Qu Yuan's Ode to the Orange also has a section that says: "Deeply rooted and difficult to move, more firmly determined, green leaves and white flowers, how delightful they are, branches with sharp thorns, fruits in the garden, green and yellow intertwined, how brilliant they are, the essence is white inside, like a path that can be taken, well-organized and suitable for cultivation, beautiful and not ugly." It is said that Qu Yuan used the qualities of the orange to symbolize his own personality, saying that he has a firm will, brilliant writing, and a beautiful essence. Now we need to save the country with personality, so when we eat oranges, we must pay attention to our own personality, and don't be inferior to oranges.

Dried Lychees from Zengcheng

— Chumei

Lychees are a famous product of Lingnan. The Guaglvk lychees of Zengcheng were formerly used as tributes during the autocratic era. Every year when the fruits ripened, the magistrate of Zengcheng presented them to the imperial family, and the common people rarely had the chance to taste this delicacy. The so-called "Guaglvk" means that there are green threads on the lychee kernels, which are like hanging paintings. This is what makes them different from ordinary lychees. No wonder Su Dongpo had the line "I would eat three hundred lychees a day, and I would not mind being a Lingnan native forever." The lychees that Su Dongpo ate were produced in Zengcheng, and his respect for them was so great.

Yang Guifei of the Tang Dynasty suffered from halitosis, and no medicine could cure it. The imperial physician said that Lingnan lychees could cure this disease. Emperor Xuanzong of Tang immediately issued an edict, and the postmaster sent them with a thousand-mile horse. After Guifei ate them, her breath was as fragrant as orchids, and since then, the tributes were continuous.

The author is from the south, and whenever lychees are in season, I must eat my fill every day. After coming to Shanghai, I have not been able to taste them, because fresh lychees transported to Shanghai have already had their skins broken and their flesh rotten, and eating them is enough to cause illness. There are dried lychees on the market, most of which are baked with fire, and the quality is dry and the taste has changed, and they are not very satisfactory.

Yesterday, I had dinner with a friend at the Weilin Restaurant next to Jing'an Temple and saw fresh dried lychees on display. I bought some to try, and they were indeed excellent products. According to Mr. Lin, an employee of the company, these dried lychees are indeed products of Zengcheng, Guangdong. A relative of his is doing business in Zengcheng, and every time lychees are on the market, he must buy the best ones at high prices and dry them completely by sun-drying with the power of sunlight. The original taste and efficacy are preserved. In previous years, they were transported to South America, and there was more demand than supply. This year, because the debts were too large, they stopped transporting them to the United States. Mr. Lin heard the news and sent a letter to his relatives, urging them to transport them all to Shanghai to share with the people of Shanghai. I unexpectedly enjoyed a great feast and ordered some to share with my relatives and friends, and they all praised them as wonderful products.

Mutton of Mao Town, Haimen

— Hao Hao

Haimen mutton has always been famous in the world, and Mao Town mutton is said to have a unique flavor. After reading this article, readers can "feast their eyes" on it.

Haimen is a medium-sized county in Jiangbei, and although it is only separated from Shanghai, which is known as the Paris of the East, by a narrow strip of water, the customs are very simple and have not been infected with extravagance. Mao Town is a large town in Haimen with prosperous commerce. During the cotton season, the villagers who carry cotton to the town like to drink a cup of wine, so mutton restaurants have sprung up in response. Of all the mutton restaurants in the town, the most famous one used to be "Shi Liujiu." His mutton was cooked properly, without any fishy smell. The mutton was cooked in "red braised," "white meat," and "clear stew." Some were cooked with vermicelli, and some were steamed with glutinous rice. The most famous mutton, of course, was the "leg tube." After cooking, add some pepper powder, dip it in sweet sauce, and add some scallion crumbs. The taste is extremely wonderful.

The mutton restaurants in Mao Town are divided into two classes. One is for the middle and lower classes to eat, and the other is exclusively for young masters and gentlemen with eight-character mustaches. The price of leg tubes is more expensive, but it only costs two or three jiao to enjoy a feast. For those wealthy gourmets, this small amount does not seem to be a big deal.

Since the death of "Shi Liujiu," more than a dozen mutton restaurants have sprung up in Mao Town. The most famous one now is "Mutton Xishi." Xishi is a proprietress. She is in her prime and is very beautiful. At the same time, her cooking skills are indeed superior to others. With this uniquely flavored mutton, plus a "Wenjun Danglu" live sign, it is no wonder that the restaurant is packed with customers.

Winter Nourishing Foods

— Chengming

Time flies so fast, and the cold season of winter has arrived again. The busy masses, in the three months of winter, generally have to take some tonics to nourish their bodies. (Except for coolies and poor people.) People with money, of course, eat some ginseng, bird's nest, and tonic medicines to nourish their bodies and replenish their energy. Ordinary people, although they do not have the ability to take ginseng tonics, must also take some ordinary nourishing materials such as milk, soy milk, and eggs. In addition, there are several kinds of foods that are suitable for winter nourishment, and they are cheap and suitable for ordinary people. Here are the methods of making them:

Astragalus Braised Mutton Astragalus Braised Mutton can be used as an appetizer or a side dish. The author personally cooks it every winter. I have been doing this for six or seven years and it does have the effect of nourishing the body and lifting the spirits. It only costs two yuan in legal currency. This method was taught by the late painter Mr. Wu Taochan. The author followed the method and cooked it for the "winter" for many years. I did not take any other tonics, and my body is very strong and no diseases have occurred. Readers of the newspaper, you may wish to try it. [Method] Use a few taels of high-quality astragalus, one yuan (all Chinese medicine stores sell it), and one piece of fresh fat mutton leg, weighing three or four pounds, which costs one yuan. Boil the astragalus in a copper pot over a fire, add three or four bowls of clear water, for one or two hours, until the medicinal juice is concentrated, drain the soup juice, and then add clear water to boil. It must be boiled four times. Cook the medicinal juice and mutton together, then add ginger slices, red dates, Shaoxing wine, rock sugar, soy sauce, and a little fennel. It should be light and not salty. After it is cooked thoroughly, then take it out of the pot. You can eat it cold or hot every day. The taste is very delicious and you do not feel the medicinal taste.

Sea Cucumber and Mutton Mutton is slightly nourishing, which everyone knows. Therefore, mutton in winter is also one of the foods rich in nutrients. It is best to use spiny sea cucumber, soak it in clear water for three or four days, then wash it clean (the water sea cucumber on the vegetable stalls has too much water and is very soft and thin, so it has lost its function), and cook it with the cooked braised mutton. The taste is incomparably delicious.

Stewed Beef Use fresh and tender beef, five or six pounds, put it in a casserole, add ginger wine, soy sauce, clear salt and other things, and use a gentle charcoal stove to simmer it for seven or eight hours, then it will be very well-cooked. All the fat juice is in the soup. If you don't like to eat beef, just eat the soup, which is also very nourishing.

Tender Chicken Tender chicken must be a hen. It is best not to cut it with iron utensils. Use a bowl to cut its throat, wait until the blood is clear, put it in a casserole, and steam it in a rice pot for one or two hours. The taste is very delicious.

Replacing the Nest: A Tale of Love and Fate

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 9: Terrible News Shocks Like a Flower Falling into Filth; Her Fragrant Shadow Frequently Visits, Her Heart is Like Willow Catkins Soaked in Mud

Guoqi was a bit stunned when he heard her words. Wasn't it you who had someone write me a letter, arranging to come today! But he didn't explain, and nodded to her in reply: "It's hot, I didn't go out. I just heard Miss Li came, so I've been waiting here." Youmei felt that his words today were much more active than usual, and he was even willing to stand and say so many polite words to a female guest. Standing in the room, she looked at the bookshelves around her and smiled, "I heard that Cousin has bought a lot more books." Guoqi laughed, "Speaking of books, it's quite funny, I don't even have enough of the books I need at hand. Please sit, please sit." Youmei smiled, "It's an honor for Cousin to let me sit in your room. It's not easy to entertain guests in the place where you read and write." Guoqi said, "You're too kind, too kind." As he spoke, he sat down on a small chair diagonally opposite her. Youmei sat on a white porcelain stool on the side of the bookshelf, slowly stroking her cheek with the index finger of her right hand, looking at the books on the bookshelf with a focused expression. Guoqi said, "Miss Li, what books do you want?" Youmei said, "Why is Qing so polite? You can just call me Cousin, or call me Youmei." Guoqi laughed, "Miss Li is so forthright, she speaks so frankly." After saying this, he felt at a loss for words, so he had to get up and pour a cup of tea himself, and handed it to her. Youmei got up, took the tea, thanked him, sat down and slowly sipped it, first smiling at Guoqi, and then becoming serious, she said, "Cousin, was there anything in the letter that Tian sent to you?" Guoqi also became serious and replied, "There was a gold ring." Originally, now we are a republic, men and women are equal, and social interaction is open, so there is no need to hide this matter. But everyone's family situation is different, so I can't talk nonsense. My relationship with that Miss Jiang is only through letters about poetry. I consider her a very loyal reader of my work. However, for someone who publishes articles, being able to have a loyal reader is no different from what the ancients called a 'soulmate of high mountains and flowing waters.' So, my feelings for Miss Jiang are only about gratitude for a kindred spirit." Youmei only sipped her tea slowly as he spoke. Even after she had finished the whole cup of tea, she still held the cup in her hand, pretending to want to drink. Finally, she said, "Menglan mentioned this to me too. Not only does she read the most Chinese books, but she also reads English books very fluently. How could she not be enamored with freedom? It's just that her background is different from ours, and she's been wearing shackles since she was a child." When Guoqi heard this, he was startled, and immediately straightened up and looked at Youmei. (107)

Jinhua Ham

— By Jian Chen

In our country, it is customary to give gifts to show respect during festivals and when relatives and friends visit. Among many gifts, Jinhua ham is considered the best. This custom flourished in the early Qing Dynasty. According to the "Zhou Chu Local Customs Records," there is the following record: "The custom of giving gifts has been around for a long time, but it was most prevalent in the early Qing Dynasty. As for gifts, Jinhua ham from Zhejiang was the best. Princes and nobles all loved it dearly. Therefore, when Manchus in the early Qing Dynasty met distinguished guests or held banquets, they would first brew famous tea and slice ham to show respect." It can be seen that Jinhua ham was very popular at that time.

As for the ham-producing areas in our country, the most famous are Jinhua and Yunnan. Yunnan Province is located in the southwest, and transportation is difficult, so not much of its produce is transported and sold to various places. Jinhua is different because of its convenient transportation and excellent products, so its products are popular throughout the country and it dominates the ham industry. Jinhua is located in central Zhejiang, slightly southwest. The Qiantang River flows through the area from Lanxi, making water transportation very convenient. In recent years, highways have been built, and land transportation is not as difficult as it used to be. Jinhua used to be under the jurisdiction of eight counties, and six of them (Jinhua, Dongyang, Yiwu, Pujiang, Yongkang, and Lanxi) all produce ham. The total annual output is thirteen thousand pieces (each weighing two hundred and ten catties), with Dongyang having the largest output, seven thousand pieces per year, followed by Yongkang, Yiwu, and other counties.

There are many names for ham, such as Southern Ham, Northern Ham, and Tea Ham, among which Tea Ham is considered the best. This product is produced in Shangjiang Village, Dongyang (Tea Ham is not produced in Jinhua, but it has always been called Jinhua Tea Ham because Dongyang was a subordinate county of Jinhua during the Qing Dynasty.) Hu Xueyan, a prominent Zhejiang merchant in the early Qing Dynasty, loved to eat it. Later, Zhejiang officials competed to purchase this product as a means of currying favor, calling it Tea Ham. As a result, various shops also prominently advertised it. Today, the name Tea Ham is known at home and abroad.

The output of Tea Ham is not large, only over three hundred pieces per year, and the price is twenty to thirty yuan more expensive per piece than Southern Ham. Ham merchants, in addition to purchasing first, second, and third-class goods, also purchase a few pieces of Tea Ham for knowledgeable buyers. Hu Hengchang in Hangzhou has a larger sales volume, so it purchases more, but the daily sales are mainly second and third-class goods, which are cheaper and not of inferior quality, just slightly less fresh. The method of making ham is very simple, that is, first select high-quality pig legs, wash them, and then salt them. After storing them for half a month, they are very salty when taken out of the jar. They should be desalted slightly before being exposed to the sun, hence the name "Fire Ham" (火腿). As for the method of making Tea Ham, that is, when putting the pig legs into the jar for salting, soak them in strong tea juice. After half a month, they can be taken out and dried in the hot sun. Then the meat will be rosy and lovely, and the taste will be fresh and delicious. The first business to specialize in Tea Ham was called Xuefang. Today, countless businesses use this name, like Lugaojian in Shanghai and Yebiji in Suzhou.

Although making ham is easy, it is difficult to preserve its taste for a long time! Because ham has been salted, it can last longer than other bland foods, but it is very susceptible to moisture. If it is slightly affected, the taste will change. Therefore, during the plum rain season, the ham should be exposed in a windy, rain-free place. If the weather is clear, it is best to dry it in the sun so that it will not be damaged by moisture.

Therefore, to ensure the good taste of ham, in addition to selecting good pig breeds and feeding them properly, it is also necessary to pay attention to proper preservation so that its taste can remain unchanged for a long time. In recent years, the ham industry has been affected by the domestic economic downturn, so business has greatly declined. Taking Hangzhou as an example, twenty years ago, seven or eight thousand pieces could be sold annually, but in recent years, only three or four thousand pieces have been sold, only half of what it used to be. If there are major domestic disasters, the number may be even less!

Commercial News

Grain: Multiple Parties Try to Absorb Supply; Speculation Drives Flour Prices Up Sharply

— Prices Rise by a Dime Limit in All Months —

Yesterday morning after the opening bell, flour prices rose sharply for all months. Although the price of foreign wheat only fell slightly by about a dime, and there was no special demand for domestic sales, speculation continued to flourish without limit. The short positions in the exchange were not factory hedging, and outside investors had already retreated, so the bulls put all their efforts into buying, creating an unprecedented surge. The market was forced to halt after rising by a dime. At the opening around 10 AM, near-term contracts rose by two or three cents, and distant-term contracts rose by four or five cents. Later, due to strong buying interest, prices rose step by step by another three or four cents. At the afternoon opening, bulls immediately raised prices, and all months had reached the dime limit. Although factories sold 60,000 to 70,000 bags, it was like a drop in the bucket and could not stop the buying frenzy. If the authorities do not take effective corrective measures, the future of the people's food supply will be greatly affected.

Wheat Itself Has No Problem; Market Increase Is Influenced by Speculative Flour; Hope to Reduce Import Tax on Foreign Wheat

Yesterday morning after the opening bell, wheat prices were initially flat and then improved. The price of foreign wheat was slightly lower, so sentiment was calm at the start. However, flour prices were manipulated by large outside investors, and the market not only did not ease but became even more heated. Therefore, after the opening, all months followed suit, rising by three, six, or seven cents. At the afternoon opening, the situation in the flour market was very serious, and short covering was strong. February and March contracts rose another three, five, or six cents. According to industry insiders, if the import tax on foreign wheat can be reduced, the fixed price is close to the sentiment of the people and will not be breached again. The current wheat market has little stock and is very high, so the market has not seen any formal delivery.

Fewer Rice Boats Arrive in Shanghai Each Day; Rice Prices in North Shanghai Rise More Sharply

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, a total of ninety ships arrived from various provinces, carrying a total of 18,400-18,500 shih of rice. Thin Dao rice still accounted for more than sixty ships. The market continued to show some vitality. However, due to the cloudy and rainy weather, which seemed to indicate snow, sentiment was firm. Sales in the local market were quite brisk, and buyers were also refreshed. About 7,000-8,000 bags of thin Dao rice and over 4,000 bags of thick Geng rice were shipped in from Tianjin, Qingdao, Yantai, and other provinces in the north. As a result, rice shops quietly raised the price of thin Dao rice by two or three jiao, thick Geng rice by one jiao and seven fen, and Du Yang Jian rice by one jiao. Yin Yuan rice was also priced higher.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, no rice boats arrived at the gates in the western section of the Suzhou River and the southern Huangpu River. Rice merchants had no rice to sell, the market was in chaos, sentiment was panicked, and rice prices soared by two or three jiao. If the detention of rice boats at Jiwang Temple is not remedied and released soon, the food supply for the entire Shanghai will be greatly affected. Yesterday, the price of Bai Geng rice soared by two or three jiao, the price of thin Dao rice rose by about three jiao, the price of Yangbu Du Ke Jian rice rose by two jiao, and the price of Yin Bian Yuan rice rose by one or two jiao. The price of other types of rice also rose by one, two, or three jiao.

Guangdong Merchants Wait and See; Early Indica Rice Market Remains Flat; Hunan Rice Can Be Shipped Directly; Impact of Tax Reduction on Foreign Rice

The market for early Indica rice has been flat for a long time. Although the prices of flour, wheat, and other grains have been rising steadily, rice prices have not been able to recover because Hunan rice is directly shipped to Guangdong Province, and the tax on foreign rice in Guangdong Province has been reduced. Therefore, Guangdong merchants have been waiting and seeing for a long time, and there has been no continued replenishment of large quantities. Although Anhui Province and other provinces have taken measures to ban shipments, market prices have not been able to rise. Yesterday, sales from Shantou and Henan provinces were brisk, and local hoarders were also active. Guangdong and northern merchants made some purchases, and market prices began to recover slightly, rising by a dime or two, depending on the variety. Yesterday, 10,000 bags of Jiangxi rice, 1,480 bags of Hunan rice, and 4,275 bags of Wenzhou, Taizhou, Ningbo, and Jiangbei rice were sold.

Soybean Cake Has Hedging Transactions

Yesterday, the soybean cake market was sluggish due to low sales. However, because standard soybean cake prices were rising sharply, and there was a profit to be made from hedging, there were hedging transactions, and prices increased. Yesterday, Sipai cake was priced at $1.90, with the January delivery contract priced at $1.93, and 3,000 pieces were traded. There were also 3,000 pieces of current cake traded.

Grain Price Statistics for November (3)

Yarn and Cotton: After Consecutive Sharp Increases, Speculators Take Profits; Sellers Surge in the Morning, Prices Fall Step by Step; Bulls Add to Positions in the Afternoon, Market Rebounds; But Overall, All Months Still Fall by More Than Two Yuan

The yarn market initially fell and then rebounded, but ultimately still fell. This was because consecutive sharp increases had prompted a large number of profit-takers to liquidate their positions. In addition, the Osaka Sanpin yarn market was lackluster, and marked yarn was more than twenty yuan higher, so some traders tended to sell. However, one merchant did not sell, and continued to add to their positions whenever the price fell. In addition, yarn stocks were unusually low, so near-term market conditions remained firm. However, current yarn sales were slightly weaker. Observing the current situation, it would not be surprising if marked yarn fell by ten yuan from its peak.

Marked Yarn Prices Increase for Both Near-Term and Distant-Term Contracts

The market for marked yarn opened lower across all months in the morning, and the momentum was weak. This was because the previous day's surge was too excessive, prompting profit-takers to close their positions. The exchange also increased the special margin to avoid danger and restricted new trading activity. In addition, as the end of the year approached, most traders closed out their positions, and the market was sluggish. Sellers came in droves, and the decline was rapid, falling step by step. As a result, all months fell by 3.6 to 4.7 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price. At the afternoon opening, near-term contracts continued to decline, while distant-term Changfeng bulls continued to add to their positions, and the market rebounded. Near-term contracts rose sharply in the second session, while distant-term contracts were flat. The third session was slightly weaker, and prices rose again until the close. However, current yarn trading became quiet. As a result, all months rose by 1.5 to 2.1 yuan compared to the morning closing price. It was found that Jinchang sold 5,400 bales, Dafeng 1,800 bales, Hengyi 1,700 bales, Mingde 1,750 bales, Hexing 4,200 bales, Yuan Yi 1,400 bales, Dachangcheng 1,050 bales, Hengchang 1,600 bales, Dachang 3,500 bales, and Renfeng 2,100 bales. Dafu bought 1,650 bales, Taixing 2,550 bales, Senkang 2,500 bales, Changfeng 5,000 bales, Runkang 3,250 bales, Yuda 3,800 bales, Yicheng 1,500 bales, Gengfeng 900 bales, Meiji 700 bales, Deda 700 bales, and Jifeng 1,000 bales. Current Yarn Rail Transport Slightly Quiet

It was found that Quan Rong and other merchants bought a total of 625 bales. The selling price fell by more than two yuan. The purchase amount of each merchant is as follows:

Near-Term Cotton Sales Show Some Squeeze

The cotton market fell in the morning and rebounded in the afternoon, showing a good trend. This was because some cotton merchants believed that the yarn market was rising, and most retail investors were buying yarn and hedging cotton, resulting in a slight squeeze in near-term sales. However, there was still no solution for the coarse velvet cotton that had been continuously hedged last month. The overseas Indian and American cotton markets continued to decline, and Shanghai cotton stocks were sufficient.

Marked Cotton Prices Increase by Half a Yuan

The market for marked cotton opened lower in the morning because the overseas Indian and American cotton markets were declining across the board, and it was rumored that Japanese merchants had purchased 2,000 bales of Indian cotton the previous day. As a result, sentiment was sluggish. At the same time, the yarn market fell, and the market situation was even worse. All months fell by 2.3 cents. Later, news of the opening of a Qingdao yarn factory slightly improved the situation. As a result, all months fell by 1.5 to 3 cents compared to the previous day's closing price. At the afternoon opening price, the market situation tightened, and the upward trend was also strong. Because the flour market was soaring, many parties were active. However, Indian cotton prices were flat and weak, and arrivals were abundant. As a result, all months rebounded by 5.5 to 6.5 cents compared to the morning closing price. It was found that Yichang sold 7,500 dan, Xinchang 4,600 dan, Dachang 1,900 dan, Dafu 1,900 dan, Juxing 3,900 dan, Fengtai and 3,200 dan, Yicheng 4,000 dan, Xinhua 3,400 dan, Yikang 3,400 dan, Xincheng 5,800 dan, Jinchang 2,200 dan, Taichang 5,900 dan, and Weifeng 5,300 dan. Tonghe bought 13,900 dan, Yuanxingchang 8,300 dan, Dachangcheng 17,600 dan, Shengyuan 6,400 dan, Weihe 5,200 dan, Daji 1,400 dan, Yuan Yi 3,400 dan, Hengyi 2,400 dan, and Meiji 3,700 dan. The highest, lowest, and closing prices for the day are listed on the left.

Current Cotton Trading Becomes Sparse

Current cotton consumption is sluggish, and factory demand is quiet. Because Indian cotton prices are approaching parity, the source is Yao cotton 685 bales, general cotton 1,360 bales, Tongzhou cotton 49.00, Shenxin Factory purchased 1,200 bales of spot goods delivered to the factory. Zhengzhou cotton 51.50, and also 100 pieces. Also, Lingxian cotton 66.00, Tongxing Factory purchased 165 pieces, and also, and also.

Yarn Exchange Further Increases Special Margin; Collects a Total of Forty-Two Yuan for December Contracts; Collects a Total of Thirty-Two Yuan for All Other Months

Because the yarn market has been rising recently, the highest peak for the December contract reached 268 yuan on the previous day. In view of the serious situation, the exchange decided to increase the special margin for cotton yarn again (starting from December 7th) to maintain stability. The special margin for cotton remained unchanged. It was found that new buyers of December cotton yarn are required to pay a special margin of 32 yuan per bale, plus the original margin of 10 yuan, for a total of 42 yuan. For all other months, a special margin of 24 yuan per bale is required, plus the original margin of 10 yuan, for a total of 32 yuan. The large increase in the margin is a new record since the establishment of the exchange.

Japanese Yarn Factories Are Buying Indian Cotton Very Actively

Although American cotton was firm last week, it failed to rise here due to the increase in new cotton movements. Export demand has recently expanded. In the Far East, due to the rise in Sanpin yarn, purchases have been very active. Lancashire is paying attention to Karachi cotton, and local yarn factories are relatively active and have hopes of resuming operations. The statistics for last week are appended below (in thousands of bales):

The prices of Mumbai yarn and cloth have increased as follows compared to last week: Shirt cloth 13 rupees 12 annas, up 4 annas; Bedding cloth 4 rupees, flat; 20-count yarn 7.75 annas, up 0.25 annas; 10-count yarn 6 annas, up 0.25 annas.

Sanpin Yarn and Cotton Prices Show Mixed Results

On the 7th, a telegram from Osaka reported that Sanpin futures yarn fell by 6 jiao to rise by 1.5 yuan, with the near-term contract at 243 yuan and the distant-term contract at 218.9 jiao. Futures cotton fell by 1.5 to 3 cents, with the near-term contract at 67.2 yuan and the distant-term contract at 68.2 yuan.

Piece Goods: High Prices of Cotton Cloth Seen Repeatedly; Shortage of Supplies from Various Sources; Sales to North and South Increase; Prices of Bleached Cloth and Flannel Surge; Factories Sell Out All Spot Goods

Yesterday, the cotton cloth market continued to be good, and selling prices remained high, unaffected by the decline in marked yarn prices. Demand from Sichuan and North China provinces increased significantly, and demand from other provinces was also good. However, the supply of cloth has been reduced due to the strike, the shortage of raw yarn, and the recent detention of rice boats, which has blocked waterways and hindered the arrival of goods from other ports. Due to these various reasons, the source of goods has been sharply reduced, so they are becoming more and more popular and new high prices are repeatedly appearing. Fine cloth and fine twill rose by 5 to 10 cents per bolt, coarse cloth and coarse twill rose by 10 to 30 cents per bolt, straight tribute, serge, and woolen cloth rose by about 10 cents per bolt, while bleached cloth and flannel were surging, rising by up to 50-60 cents per bolt. In the past two days, all spot goods and goods arriving from other ports from various factories have been purchased by various merchants. There are still many who have pre-purchased goods for this month. Tianjin merchants purchased more than 500 pieces of white flannel, serge, and woolen cloth, and Sichuan merchants purchased more than 400 pieces of straight tribute, woolen cloth, blue cloth, colored twill, and fine cloth. Chunling goods from Guangzhong, Hongzhang, Huayang, Liming, and other factories, and plain silk are being sold successively for this month and January, totaling one thousand several hundred boxes, mostly plain silk in plain colors, purchased by merchants from Sichuan and Hunan.

Overcoat Fabrics Sell Well

Woolen fabrics have been selling very well recently. As it is cold in winter, woolen fabrics are all in season. Heavy overcoat fabrics are widely sold by tailors. Sales of plain, thick fabrics, riding breeches, thick serge, and thick overcoat fabrics are particularly strong. Long-haired camel wool, 30-count colored riding breeches, navy blue melton, plain, thick fabrics, Jinshan and silk-glossed feather yarn, horsehair lining, and horse bristle sleeves have all been particularly popular recently. Goods are in short supply and prices are rising. Tailors have been actively replenishing their stocks, resulting in supply falling short of demand.

Finance: Bulls Strongly Resisting Gold Prices; Fluctuates Midway; Ultimately Increases Eight Jiao

The gold market rose yesterday. The market was stable as soon as trading started. In addition, the large short positions were being covered, stimulating buying and increasing the price. There was also some selling by the bulls and some fluctuations. In the morning, the overseas silver market saw the English market rise and the American market remain flat. The forward silver price in Montevideo rose by 4 to 6.5 percent. The exchange rate contracted, and the price of raw gold in London rose by one penny. The Central Bank's official rate was announced, with the English and American markets both flat. The customs gold unit rose by 4 percent. The standard price for gold was raised to 1,154.4 yuan. The morning opening was slightly higher, and there were fluctuations after the opening. Although large and spot firms provided some supply, it did not have much impact. The shorts took advantage of the low prices to cover their positions, and prices rebounded. The official rate of HSBC was announced, with the English and American markets both flat, with the price at 5.1 yuan. There was still a lot of struggle at this time. Later, as the shorts continued to cover their positions, and the sellers came to buy, the silver balance tax was announced, rising by half a cent, so it was pulled up. Large firms took advantage of the high prices to supply, and prices fell once, but sentiment remained stable. The afternoon was still stable. Although the bulls sold off some positions in the after-market, the large short positions continued to be strongly covered, and the trend remained firm. The price of Indian silver also contracted by three annas. The day's market conditions are recorded below.

The morning opening was at 1,155 yuan, 1 jiao better than last Saturday. Qiafeng, Yongda, and Dafeng Heng sold, retreating from 5.1 yuan to 4.9 yuan. Tongtaichangxiangfeng came in and rose to 5.3 yuan. Qiafeng, Yongda, and Dacheng took advantage of the high prices to sell. The official rate of HSBC was announced, with the English and American markets both flat, retreating to 5.1 yuan. Tongtaichang still entered, and Dafeng Heng Qiafeng Yong sold, and there was more trading. Later, Tongtaichang Qiafeng Yong Yuanmao Yong entered, and the silver balance tax was announced, rising by half a cent, rising to 5.8 yuan. Jinfeng Yongda Dafeng Heng Heng Yu Qingfa Yong sold, retreating to 5.4 yuan. Qiafeng Yong paid again, rising to 5.7 yuan, and Dadecheng sold. The closing price was 1,155.6 yuan. The price was slightly tired after closing.

The after-market opened at 1,155.6 yuan, and Yuanting sold, retreating to 5.5 yuan. Tongtaichang came in, rising to 5.7 yuan. Fuxing Yong sold, retreating to 5.5 yuan. Qiafeng Yong and Tongtaichang still entered, and the closing price rose to 1,155.7 yuan.

The closing price was the standard gold price of the Central Bank, rising to 1,154.4 yuan, with a closing price of 11 yuan. The January account was 1,156 yuan. The morning water replenishment was 1,154 yuan. The spot market was stable, and there were few sellers. The Tianjin goods were priced at an additional 13.25 yuan, and the Chichi buying price was an additional 11 yuan, and the selling price was 15 yuan, but there were no counterparties.

Trading in the field was still flat. Tongtaichang Yuanmao Yongxiangfeng, etc. were on the buying side, and Yuanheng Fuxing Yong Dafeng Heng Yida Dadecheng Futai Heng Heng Yu Shengyuan Yong Yuanfeng Yong Shenyu, etc. were on the selling side. Jinfeng Yongqiafeng Yong entered and then exited.

It was found that the market conditions were stable throughout the day. The morning opening was at 1,155 yuan, and the final closing was at 1,155.7 yuan. The highest price was 1,155.8 yuan, and the lowest price was 1,154.9 yuan, with a fluctuation of 9 jiao. As a result, it rose by 8 jiao compared to the previous closing price. There were 5,026 January term chips, with 28 long parties and 27 short parties. The number of transactions was 413 in the first session and 308 in the second session.

Yesterday, 28 public orders were released by Dafeng Heng and received by Qiafeng Yong, with a closing price of 1,153 yuan, and the chips for this month have been temporarily cleared.

Sugar Market: Domestic Cotton Red Pieces are Scarce, Leading to Price Increases

Yesterday, the sugar market was stable. The guild's price for No. 24 coarse granulated white sugar spot was 21 yuan and 55 cents, with a slight outflow, up 2.5 cents. Re-export goods were quoted at 6 yuan, 1 dime, and 2 cents, up 2 cents. There were no significant changes in the spot and re-export prices of Dongbai No. 489. The price of cotton white sugar from our factory also remained the same. The Chaozhou merchants opened more than 30 packages of cotton red, and because the value to storage are all scarce, prices increased by 30 to 40 cents, with transactions at 15 yuan and 60 cents.

The joint venture company held its first tender this week for Guangdong sugar, with a total quota of more than 11,400 bags. The bid price remained unchanged. 920 bags of coarse white sugar from the Shunde Factory's Five Rams brand were sold at 21 yuan and 30 cents; 270 bags from the Xinshi brand were sold at 21 yuan and 10 cents; and 10 bags from Shantou were sold at 20 yuan and 90 cents.

Foreign Exchange: British and American Currencies Tight

Yesterday, in the foreign exchange market, the British and American currencies were tight while the Japanese Yen eased. Banks were willing to absorb them. According to morning reports from overseas, the London long-term and short-term rates both rose by 1.25. The New York silver market was closed due to a strike. The forward silver price in Monterrey rose by 4.0% to 6.5%. The price of raw gold in London rose by 3 pence. The British pound weakened against the US dollar by 0.25, and remained unchanged against the French Franc. The US dollar weakened against the British pound by 0.21875, and weakened against the French Franc by 0.1875. The Central Bank's official rates were announced: both British and American currencies remained level. The customs gold unit rose by 4%. The foreign exchange market opened in the morning with the near-term selling price of the British pound at 1 shilling, 2 and 53125/625 pence. The US dollar was at 29.6875 yuan, which was a slight increase compared to the previous closing. The British pound was level, while the US dollar tightened by 0.03125. After the opening, Chinese merchants sold off Eastern currencies, while Japanese banks strongly supported the market. Banks released near-term US dollars, while the Sin Fung Foreign Firm bought them. The HSBC bank's official rates were announced: both British and American currencies remained level, and there was still demand in the market. The White Silver Equalization Tax was announced, rising by 0.5%. Banks made slight supplemental purchases, while Japanese banks continued to absorb. The trend began to shift from loose to level, and banks also engaged in reciprocal transactions. The market hovered around midday. Although there were telegraphic sales from Hong Kong in the afternoon, banks generally maintained their positions and there were no major changes. The initial decision on Indian silver was to remain unchanged, but the second decision reported a small increase of 3 annas. The final decision was revised. The closing selling price of the British pound was 1 shilling, 2 and 5625/5 pence. The US dollar was at 19.6875 yuan, which was a slight increase compared to the previous closing. Both the British and American currencies showed a slight tightening. The transactions for today will be recorded below.

The British pound opened in the morning with the near-term buying price at 1 shilling, 2 and 53125/5625 pence. New and old currencies were sold to Macao at a spot price of 5625. Cheng Chin bought spot goods at 5625. Citibank sold to Jardine Matheson January at ½ pence. In the afternoon, Hong Kong sold to Shanghai January at ½ pence, and spot goods at 5625. Macao bought the first half of December at 53125. The closing selling price was spot goods at 1 shilling, 2 and 53125 pence, December at the same price, January at ½ pence, February at 46875, and March at 4375. The buying price was slightly higher.

The US dollar opened in the morning with a near-term selling price of 29.6875 yuan. Citibank put in December at 625. Shanghai Citibank sold to Sin Fung. Citibank bought the first half of January at 625. Cheng Chin bought December at the same price. Chase sold to Citibank. HSBC sold to Shanghai spot goods at 6875. Overseas Chinese put in December at 625. The midday closing price for near-term selling was 29.6875 yuan. In the afternoon, Hong Kong sold to Citibank January at 625. Hong Kong sold to Macao Citibank December at 6875. Banque Belge pour l'Etranger (Belgian Bank for Foreign Trade) Macao put in February at ½ yuan. The closing selling price was spot goods at 29.6875 yuan, December at 625, January at 5625, February at ½ yuan, and March at 4375. The buying price was increased by 0.0625.

Securities and Public Bond Market Atmosphere Unusually Ordinary

The difference between high and low is between one and two jiao.

Yesterday, the market situation for the public bonds on the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange became even more sluggish. The market fluctuations were also extremely ordinary. The current situation is chaotic, and the people's spirits are increasingly scattered. Large investors are extremely lacking in participation. Even the transactions of retail investors have decreased. The comparison between the high and low prices of the entire day's market did not exceed one or two jiao. The volume of transactions was also sparse. Such a quiet phenomenon is rare. The market price fluctuations are becoming increasingly sluggish. In a state of fluctuation, it is still not easy to develop a trend. The market trend yesterday only saw more selling from retail investors when the market opened in the morning, and the selling of No. 77 and No. 35 was slightly more enthusiastic. The market price fell by one, two, or three jiao across the board. The remaining three trading sessions were extremely stable. Each household only supplied three or five million in capital for supply and demand, which could manipulate the rise and fall of the market situation. The market price also only had a difference of jiao. Major buyers absorbed No. 5, No. 50, and No. 72 in comparison. No. 14 and No. 35 had selling, but the amount was also limited. The result of the whole day was a slight decrease of five cents to two jiao across the board. The total number of transactions was 3.87 million yuan. The comparison of the rise and fall of the highs and lows is listed on the left (unit yuan, transaction unit hundred yuan)

Oil Market: After the Release of New Asphalt, the Rise of Macheng Heavy Jing Oil is Still Difficult to Ease. Although Lanyang Oil is Cheap, its Moisture Content is High. Hwobon Oil is Highly Priced, Only for Emergencies.

Since the old asphalt was searched and collected everywhere by foreign firms, it has been sold out everywhere. Although the new oil has also entered the market, it has not yet become prosperous. As a result, there has been a gap between the new and old oils, and production has been interrupted for more than half a month. Although the production volume is gradually increasing, the demand for candles has also begun. Therefore, the supply in the markets of Hankou and Shanghai is still far from meeting demand. In the Hankou market, only 70 to 100 pieces of Macheng oil arrive every day. In terms of sales, even if 2,000 to 3,000 pieces arrived, it would not be enough to distribute. The gap between arrival and sales is so huge. It is unknown when there will be a hope for relaxation. Five years ago, when the price of heavy Jing oil rose to more than 40 yuan, there was no such phenomenon in the market. Although there was a lack of continuity between the new and old oils, there was always a constant supply, but the time interval was never as long as this time. Recently, the Macheng oil arriving in the Hankou market has been supplied and packaged by various gangs as it arrives. In the future, when the market opens, it is feared that it will not be possible to sell it for less than 20 yuan per dan. The price of heavy Jing oil has opened at 21.8 yuan per piece, which, when combined with the arrival in the Shanghai market, is already at 24.5 or 6 yuan. The trend is imminent. It is already a great favor to be able to distribute dozens of pieces. Therefore, local merchants in Shanghai have discussed selling it for 25.5 yuan. The minimum price must also be 25 yuan. Macheng oil must also be at 23.5 or 6 yuan. However, due to the lack of supply, it is generally a rare and odd phenomenon. It is only heard that Jinlan and other places in eastern Zhejiang can produce more than 200 pieces every day. The oil previously sold off has been settled and shipped completely. There is now a slight surplus of existing oil, and the market is gradually trending towards peace. One piece has slightly eased to 23 yuan for Lanyang delivery. However, because the new oil inevitably contains moisture, it still seems to be more expensive when combined with Jing oil. Although the demand for goods in Shanghai is strong, it is still waiting and watching. The price of Hwobon oil in western Zhejiang is the highest, requiring more than 25 yuan per dan. Even if there are a few transactions, it is only for emergencies, and it is not enough to be considered a standard market. Moreover, the local annual yield is extremely poor. The cost of new oil must be 26 or 7 yuan. Therefore, what is currently sold is only old oil. It is also heard that the number of old oil reserves is greater than the amount of new oil produced this year. Because the production of new oil is only one-tenth of the previous year, the local area is hoarding and speculating.

Refined Tung Oil for Export: Refining is Fast at Eight Jiao. The Spot Oil Price in Hankou Rises Again.

The white tung oil route for foreign firms in the Hankou market has always been uninterrupted throughout the year. The quantity varies, and there is no fixed time. Since the new oil was released this year, only a small amount of spot oil has been handled in the autumn season. There are not many futures for November. The quantity is slightly larger in December, January, and February. Therefore, exports in October were very sparse. It is estimated that it will not exceed 2,000 tons last month. It is likely that the market will begin to prosper this month. However, because there was no autumn rain this year, and the winter was sunny, the water volume of the Yangtze River was extremely shallow in the upper reaches, which has been unprecedented in decades. The oil from various producing areas in Sichuan and western Hubei could not be shipped out. Only a small amount could be loaded from the Changde area of Hunan Province due to the shallow water, and it was very delayed. Therefore, the source of supply in the Hankou market was unusually sparse. During this severe winter, according to past examples, it is the time of peak production, and the market should be in a state of easing and decline. However, the arrival of goods is so meager that it is impossible to fall. Fortunately, the spot oil taken by each foreign firm is only a small amount of dozens of tons, so the price has not risen sharply. Otherwise, it is unknown how the market would change. However, the time for settlement of the previously sold futures is approaching. Sellers may have already supplemented their positions to offset the delivery. If the incoming goods are delayed, the spot oil will inevitably be squeezed temporarily. Currently, the futures handled by various foreign firms are mostly for February and March. The price is 48.5 yuan to 48.2 yuan per dan, including gross profit and foreign regulations, and transactions are taking place one after another. The quantity is also not small. However, according to a telegram received in Shanghai from Hankou yesterday, the spot oil has been increased to 50 yuan. This shows the shortage of spot oil. Since the establishment of the Plant Oil Factory of the Ministry of Industry in Shanghai, all exported oil must be refined by the factory. Work has now begun. The oil merchants in Shanghai who are engaged in export trade have also negotiated with the factory. Therefore, the oil that has arrived recently has been sent to the factory for storage. According to reports, the shipment is very fast. The refining fee is calculated at 8 jiao in national currency, which is more than double the amount required for self-refining in the past. Oil merchants have no choice. The foundation for the control of oil inspection and foreign trade has been established. Observing the situation, there will be more advanced measures in the near future.

Silk and Tea: Indian Firms are Selling Silk Especially Well. Chekiang Silk's Supply is Not Enough to Meet Demand

Yesterday, the Yokohama silk market continued to see a small decline. Spot goods fell by 10 yuan, and futures fell by 19 yuan. There was no market in the United States. The sales of white filature and French silk remained sluggish and there was little development in recent days. Indian firms are selling silk especially well. The Urgent Need for Protecting the Soldiers at the Suiyuan Front Line (Part 1)

——Dr. Pang Jingzhou's Lecture——　Recorded by Jiang Huiming

Reporter's Foreword

Mr. Pang Jingzhou has just returned from studying in the New World. He came back at a time when the smoke of war was rising in Suiyuan like a beacon. As everyone cared about the survival of the nation at the front line, Mr. Pang flew to the front line with enthusiastic patriotic social leaders from Shanghai to conduct on-site observations and to comfort the soldiers at the forefront on behalf of the citizens of Shanghai. The news was published in the newspapers and everyone knew it in great detail.

However, from a medical perspective, what we urgently need to understand is the situation of the rescue at the front and what kind of needs there are. The importance of this issue is not only a concern for people in the medical and pharmaceutical circles across the country, but also an urgent hope for all Chinese people. In order to understand this issue urgently, the reporter invited Mr. Pang to publicly explain it in the public medical and pharmaceutical lecture of the Sino-Western Radio Station on December 1, the day before Mr. Pang went to Beiping. Mr. Pang agreed to our request and gave a very brief speech from his busy schedule. The audience must have been very clear. In order to inform people across the country for research purposes, we have recorded the points about rescue in Mr. Pang's speech and published them in this magazine so that people in the medical and pharmaceutical circles can have a comprehensive plan and preparation at this time to meet the urgent needs of the front line.

1. General Concepts from Suiyuan

The country is in imminent danger, and only resistance can lead to survival. This has become the central belief of almost everyone in every important position on the national defense front line. Every soldier fighting is a man who deeply understands righteousness. The expression of the spirit of loyalty and courage is really unrestrained, which makes people feel unspeakable excitement and optimism.

The biggest purpose of this trip, on the one hand, was to comfort; on the other hand, I was entrusted by the Red Cross and went with Mr. Yan Fuqing to survey the local situation and plan rescue work. We have this additional mission, so our eyes on Suiyuan also concern the design of the Suiyuan rescue work.

The rescue agencies there are really too poor. Apart from a relatively complete Belgian hospital, the rest are few and far between. Although Mr. Yan Baichuan of Shanxi ordered the local Chuanzhi Hospital authorities to plan the rescue of the Suiyuan war, there are many places that need our assistance and supplementation from the rear.

As everyone knows, Northerners have Northern strength, especially in Suiyuan. Some places are really boundless deserts, with no people in sight for miles. It is unknown how many miles you have to walk to reach a village. Under these circumstances, it is also difficult for the location of the rescue team to have a close response with the soldiers at the front line. Fortunately, the brave men of the North have a spirit of perseverance and courage. If they have minor injuries, they never want to take a break. They tear up their clothes, wrap up their wounds themselves, and they still want to fight desperately forward! We know that medicine tells us that no matter what kind of wound, it is necessary to strictly disinfect and wrap it with appropriate symptoms to be safer. However, the wounds that the brave men at the front encounter do not have disinfecting medicines to apply, nor do they have disinfecting gauze or bandages... for them to wrap up; the tools they use to cover their wounds are only the belts on their bodies. On the belts that are covered with flying sand and splashed with dirt, letting them wrap the wounds, how dangerous is this? Not to mention anything else, just talking about tetanus bacteria, which live in the soil, in case the mud splashes on the belts, and the belts happen to have tetanus bacteria, this minor injury will turn into a life-threatening serious illness, which is self-evident!

Therefore, from this aspect, we have a clear concept: we believe that the loyalty and courage of the soldiers at the front are extraordinary; the danger of the soldiers at the front is also extraordinary! They are not only constantly guarding against the enemy's harm; at the same time, if they are lucky enough to survive small injuries, they do not know how serious the hidden crisis is. How can we not try to protect their precious lives?

2. The Simplest First Aid Method Most Needed at the Front Line

We understand the environment of the front line, and understand the spirit and pain of the soldiers at the front. How should we try to rescue them? When I was on the return trip, I discussed with Mr. Yan Fuqing and others, and everyone thought that the only way was to supply a kind of first-aid kit. In the current process of the Suiyuan War, a complete rescue organization and rescue talent are of course very needed: but in fact, it cannot be done completely. The brave men of the North, that kind of extraordinary and strong personality, never take minor injuries to heart, so it is necessary to design a simple emergency medicine kit, and give each person one to carry with them, which is more reasonable and safer than using clothes to wrap wounds.

Immediately, we took this plan back to Shanghai and discussed it with the Shanghai Rescue Public Group. We are very grateful for everyone's sympathy, and people in the pharmaceutical industry are willing to undertake the production of 100,000 sets, which is really a happy thing. As for the things prepared in the rescue medicine kit, they are as follows.

A small bottle of dilute tincture of iodine, a piece of sea iodine gauze, a piece of mercuric chloride gauze, a roll of bandage, a small roll of band-aid, a piece of triangular bandage, two safety pins, and two painkillers.

The medicines and supplies in this first-aid kit are probably these. However, our original plan was to put these supplies in a paper bag with instructions printed on the outside, but we were afraid that it would be inconvenient to carry or easily broken, so we decided to use a cigarette tin, store the medicines inside, tie a rope on the outside, and paste the instructions on it, so that the soldiers can hang it on their belts and apply it easily, and it can also maintain the disinfection inside the can.

When I say this, I remember another sentence, everything needs to "adapt to the times", and it is probably not wrong to do so. (To be continued)

The Construction of Tomorrow's Nursing Profession in China (Part 2)

— Li Lingdong

Therefore, we should regard the problem of internship for nursing students as one where various courses are taken during the first two years of training, and then during the final year or half year, students return to the wards for full-time internship. This will allow nursing students to have a good effect on their service spirit and physical health, and will suit the purpose of educating talents. However, the daily courses should be based on the standard of equal emphasis on "theory" and "practice." Simply talking on paper in books is equivalent to the situation of "empty valleys transmitting sounds." Practice classrooms should be established for practice. If there is too much emphasis on practice without understanding theory, it will also create a deformed "apprenticeship." I hope that the nursing community will not ignore the problem of internship for nursing students again!

The subject of Chinese language should focus on applied writing so that it can be suitable for practical application when serving society. Therefore, a nurse is often confused about correspondence, condolences, petitions, announcements, reports, etc. in society and does not know where to start writing. This is entirely due to the lack of sufficient practice at school. In the future, the subject of Chinese language must not focus solely on studying the works of ancient masters.

We believe that it is necessary to add the subject of physics and chemistry because nurses' work is closely related to physics and chemistry. What we encounter in daily life is all within the circle of scientific medicine. If we have no knowledge base of physics and chemistry, how can we understand the principles of medical treatment and diagnosis? Physics and chemistry are the mother of medical science and the foundation of nursing science. Because we cannot deny that physics and chemistry are the mother of medical science, we cannot oppose that it is the foundation of nursing science. Physics and chemistry should be a compulsory and major subject in the nursing curriculum.

Fifth, concentrated training for nurses is the driving force for transforming old lives into new lives.

We should plan for the reform and improvement of nursing education for tomorrow and forget that there are already more than 9,000 nurses who have graduated. Without training, there will be great resistance to reforming nursing education for tomorrow because these more than 9,000 nurses have not been baptized by the new education. Their thinking is stubborn, and their work skills are stagnant. At the same time, they always occupy a leading position in nursing schools, hospitals, and society. They have not been able to understand the new educational trends, and the system for managing students is still the apprentice method. If you think that the leadership is in such a situation, the promotion of nursing education for tomorrow cannot be discussed on the same day.

If we train these more than 9,000 nurses in new nursing education and transform their old lives into new lives, we can turn the "resistance" to the advancement of nursing education into a "driving force" for promoting nursing education. From this, we can see that training past nurses is an urgent matter.

How do we train them? The principle is that it does not hinder the work of the original service unit and that the training can be popularized in a short period of time. The training time for each course is six months. The country is divided into 30 locations, and each location recruits 50 people. In just three years, more than 9,000 nurses can be trained in new nursing education. At the same time, if there are three nurses in a hospital, only one needs to be trained for half a year, which will not hinder the work they are responsible for.

Sixth, "training" and "education" should be implemented together to seek the source of the development of the nursing career.

The combination of "training" and "education" has had a huge shock in modern educational thought. In the past, we only knew how to develop in academic knowledge, and we did not pay much attention to the guidance of character. As a result, students became frivolous, vain, extravagant, and dissipated, their spirits were scattered, and the more knowledge they gained, the more they helped them do bad things, harming society and becoming a scourge to mankind. Therefore, the education community today believes that the importance of "training and education" is no less than "education." Therefore, the facilities of "training and education" are being promoted by the national education community with all its strength.

The implementation of "training" and "education" in nursing education is more urgent than in other professions. Students in nursing schools are different from other schools. They have to work in the ward step by step. The ward is a microcosm of a part of society and is very close to society. Because of personal lack of knowledge and poor character, it can affect the reputation of the entire hospital and affect the future of the entire school. Therefore, how can we ignore the simultaneous implementation of "training" and "education" in nursing education today? Conclusion

To sum up, if these opinions on building China's nursing career can be implemented, China's nursing career will definitely prosper after only three years. The nursing profession originated with Miss Nightingale, but the establishment of nursing as a school-based career is also due to the efforts of the Chinese nursing community, which has set an example for the world's nursing career and won a place of glory for the country. May my Chinese medical and pharmaceutical community and nursing community comrades strive for it.

Spitting into a Handkerchief

— Song Ke San

As long as you observe carefully, you can see at any time and anywhere that Chinese people blindly follow the movements of foreigners. High-heeled leather shoes, corsets, knee-length skirts, and other unhygienic habits, which one of them was not learned from foreigners? However, these habits only hinder one's own health and have nothing to do with others. The most harmful to public health is spitting into a handkerchief!

Spitting all over the ground is a bad habit of Chinese people. When Zeng Jize and Li Hongzhang were envoys to foreign countries, they were despised by foreigners for spitting anywhere on the ship, leaving an indelible stain on the international community. Since then, Chinese people have gradually realized that spitting is unhygienic! Also, in order to imitate the actions of foreigners, they changed from spitting all over the ground to spitting into handkerchiefs! Indeed, spitting all over the ground has the risk of spreading germs, but the phlegm on the ground will kill some germs after being exposed to sunlight. Those that have not been killed are dispersed in all directions by the dust, indirectly infecting people, and not everyone is necessarily infected. As for spitting into a handkerchief? The harm is even greater! After spitting, the spitter puts the handkerchief in his arms. After the body temperature evaporates, it dries immediately. At this time, the germs on the phlegm are clearly attached to the clothes. When the spitter takes it out for the second time, he folds the side that has been spit on. Between one fold and one stack, aren't the germs on the handkerchief immediately dispersed in the surrounding four, within the air? At this time, the person on the opposite side is invisibly exposed to the risk of direct infection between one breath and one word. At the same time, there is no place on the hands and thighs of the spitter that is free of germs. As long as his hand touches any object at will, the object will have the presence of germs. Isn't it becoming a medium for germs? How dangerous is it to be with such a germ-carrying person!

Of course, phlegm should be spit into a spittoon with sterilizing water. Putting down the spittoon and spitting into a handkerchief as a modern thing, isn't this harmful and self-harming modern thing blind obedience? You must know that spitting into a handkerchief is a last resort because you have to spit into a handkerchief when you encounter a place without a spittoon! But at least you have to bring a few more handkerchiefs. One handkerchief can only be used once, and it must be boiled with sterilizing water after use. I would like to ask how many people can do this in reality? I have seen people spitting into handkerchiefs, and one handkerchief is covered with thick phlegm! It is as hard as if it has been pasted with paste. They still continue to spit and even praise themselves as hygienic experts. This kind of hygiene can only be explained by himself.

Some people say that spitting all over the ground is like setting up cannons on the ground to bomb people. I think spitting into a handkerchief is like taking out a gun and shooting people in the face. Cannons bombing people doesn't mean everyone will be bombed. Shooting people with a gun means that the person on the opposite side can hardly escape. As for the two disasters, which is direct, which is indirect, which is inevitable, and which is accidental, it is not necessary to be wise to know it.

In short, not all foreign habits are worth learning. Blindly following others will always be greatly fooled, and spitting into a handkerchief is just one example!

General Knowledge of Eye, Ear, Nose, and Throat Diseases

— Tang Renjin

(111) General Symptoms of Laryngeal Diseases

The general symptoms of laryngeal diseases are mainly three: (1) change in voice, (2) difficulty in breathing, and (3) coughing. These three symptoms are common occurrences in any type of laryngeal disease. I will elaborate on them separately as follows:

(1) Change in voice – The voice becomes turbid, impure, or loses its original tone when speaking. This is what is called hoarseness. In severe cases, it can lead to complete loss of voice, known as aphonia. In order to produce a normal voice, we must have four conditions: First, the airflow vibrating the vocal cords must have a certain strength and speed; Second, the glottis must be completely closed; Third, the vocal cords must be tense; Fourth, the vocal cords must vibrate freely. If the vocal cords themselves or their surroundings develop lesions, or if the movement system of the vocal cords is impaired, these four conditions will inevitably be incomplete, and the patient will experience changes in voice accordingly. This often occurs in cases of severe bodily weakness, vocal cord overuse, inflammatory congestion, infiltration, ulceration, tumor formation, and diseases of the vocal cord muscles and their motor nerves.

(2) Breathing difficulty – Breathing difficulty is mostly caused by narrowing of the larynx. Its main causes are generally swelling of the larynx or its surroundings, cellulitis, tumors (such as goiter, aortic aneurysm, or cancer), foreign bodies, laryngospasm, and paralysis of the glottis-opening muscles. If the breathing difficulty is mild, there is no apparent abnormality when at rest. Only during physical exertion or emotional excitement does shortness of breath occur. If the breathing difficulty reaches a high degree, there is a risk of suffocation and death.

(3) Cough – Coughing is also a common symptom of laryngeal diseases. Coughing can occur voluntarily or reflexively. When there is disease in the posterior wall of the larynx, the arytenoid cartilage folds, and the area below the vocal cords, it is easy to trigger persistent coughing attacks. If secretions are coughed up, it is called a wet cough; otherwise, it is called a dry cough. The tone of the cough varies, so there are distinctions such as hoarse, barking, metallic, flute-like, and silent coughs.

(112) Laryngitis

Laryngitis has both acute and chronic forms. However, based on clinical evidence, acute cases are more common, especially during the dry season of early winter. Therefore, I will focus on the acute form here.

The causes of acute laryngitis are generally chemical, mechanical, and thermal stimuli. For example, colds, overuse of the vocal cords, air containing dust or toxic gases, and excessive use of tobacco and alcohol can all cause this condition. Young men are most susceptible. Onset is often rapid, often accompanied by pharyngitis. Secretions increase. The voice becomes hoarse. The larynx itches. In severe cases, there is a burning sensation or sore throat. Sometimes, bloody sputum is coughed up, causing patients to panic, mistaking it for hemoptysis. If we examine the larynx with a laryngoscope, we will see general redness and swelling of the laryngeal mucosa, especially in the epiglottis, aryepiglottic folds, vocal cords, false vocal cords, and subglottic mucosa. In addition, vocal cord movement disorders often occur.

The treatment for acute laryngitis involves strictly avoiding stimulation from tobacco and alcohol, avoiding talking, cold, and dust. Regular bowel movements are also important. All drinks and foods should be warm. As for internal medications and local treatments, they must be prescribed and administered by a doctor for proper care.

Introducing a New Type of Medical Publication (Part 1)

— Shou Yuan

— Modern Medical Translation Series —

Speaking of which, it was already three or four years ago. That was when I was editing the medical and pharmaceutical supplement of the Chen Bao (Morning Post). At that time, I and my colleagues who wrote articles for the medical journal had a common feeling about the domestic medical and pharmaceutical publications: we thought that the content of most domestic medical journals was somewhat mediocre: too superficial for doctors to read, with little reference value; and honestly, too profound for the general public to understand. If we really want to do something for China's medical culture, it is necessary to expand our organization (we had a small organization at that time that hosted the medical journal, called the Public Medical and Pharmaceutical Society), gather medical colleagues who are interested in medical culture work, and roughly divide the medical publications into two levels, and jointly do some "two-level system" of textual work.

How to divide medical publications into two levels? What is the "two-level system" of medical writing?

We made the medical knowledge publications for the general public to read even more simple and popular, and tried our best to make the text and meaning of the text popular, so that the general public could understand and easily digest them. Because this is the work of imparting knowledge to the public. On the other hand, when we write medical articles for medical colleagues to refer to, we need to be more specialized; but not the specialization of simply copying old books, but specialized articles with fresh materials and insights from each person.

Regarding these two textual works, we also had a concrete plan at that time: for the former general indoctrination work, in addition to the existing medical supplements, we would reorganize them and plan to publish several kinds of popular series as medical knowledge reading materials for the general public; as for the latter's work policy, because it is specifically for medical colleagues to refer to, it seemed more difficult, so we turned the idea of ​​this textual work to the aspect of translation. Because if we ourselves run a medical magazine or other publications, to write fresh and insightful things on a regular basis, honestly, we don't have that much fresh material, and we don't have that many insightful texts to write. Translation is certainly a kind of introduction work. If we can gather some colleagues who understand the languages ​​of various countries, jointly subscribe to several copies of excellent medical publications from various advanced countries, and think about doing this job of introducing and translating matchmaking, it might be easier. If we can solicit comrades and improve the organization, we really want to run a publication for this specialized textual work, focusing on the introduction work of translation. This is indeed a very good kind of spiritual food for general clinical doctors. Isn't this a meaningful work that is unique?

However, the result was that, due to the limitations of various people's living environment, economic situation, talented comrades, and other such realistic conditions, this plan was never realized, and the idea was simply turned over and finished. When the Chen Bao (Morning Post) was suspended for some reason, even our original medical and pharmaceutical weekly column on that newspaper had to be declared "dead." Since then, our interest and enthusiasm for writing medical articles has also faded invisibly, and we have no more thoughts to think about or the courage to realize the various plans we initially made.

Recently, we received very satisfying unexpected good news. Not long ago, I received a new type of medical publication edited by Dr. Yang Yuanji, called "Modern Medical Translation Series." I hurriedly finished reading it, and then I immediately remembered this episode of three or four years ago. At the same time, after reading it, I had such a feeling: Dr. Yang's work is exactly in line with one of my ideal works a few years ago. This work is precisely what is urgently needed in the current medical field.
